(Ord. No. 950, § V, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016) 
Cross reference— Curfew, §§ 36-82 et seq.  
Sec. 6-23. - Penalty for failure to pay occupation tax. 
The city manager or designee is authorized to seal any recreation or amusement machine, or pool or billiard table on which the occupation tax has not been paid. The permit department is authorized to charge a fee of $5.00 per machine for the release of any recreation or amusement machine, pool or billiard table that is sealed as provided above for nonpayment of the occupation tax. The owner and/or operator shall be responsible should any seal affixed in the name of the city be broken, and anyone who removes from the location any recreation or amusement machine, pool or billiard table shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor under the laws of the state. 
(Ord. No. 950, § VI, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-24. - Inspections. 
The city manager shall appoint or designate an authorized representative to make periodic inspections of premises licensed under this article to determine compliance with the building provisions, applicable code provisions and any other ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. No. 950, § VII, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-25. - License required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person or business entity that owns an amusement center, save and except local religious, charitable or education organizations authorized under the laws of the state, to operate such business within the city without first having obtained an appropriate license from the city permit department. The initial application for license shall be made with the city permit department and renewed thereafter on or before the anniversary date of each succeeding year. Whoever shall violate this section shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor under this Code. 
(Ord. No. 950, § VIII, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-26. - Fee. 
There is levied an annual license fee per location on each person or business entity that owns an amusement center within the city. The city of permit department is authorized to collect this annual license fee, which shall be due and payable on January 1st of each year or upon commencing business. In the event that a person or business entity seeks to increase the amount of machines during the course of the year, an additional payment of a license and occupational fee will be due and payable immediately. The city will be paid under the guidelines set forth herein. The annual license and occupational fee for such business shall be based $1,000.00 per machine. 
(Ord. No. 950, § IX, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-27. - Nuisance declared. 
Because of the rapid proliferation of such businesses in the city and the observed congestion, late hours, potential for being an attractive nuisance to minors and the questioned legality of such activities, the city council hereby finds that a further proliferation and concentration of such businesses constitutes a nuisance to the health, safety and welfare of the city. Accordingly, subsequent to the passage of the ordinance from which article derives, no license will be issued for any such establishment unless such is at least 300 feet in a direct line from any of its public entrances to the nearest property line of a church, hospital, or school. Any business-entity currently operating under a valid license issued under a prior ordinance and prior to the passage of the ordinance from which this article derives shall be permitted to continue in operation, provided, however, if they should cease operations for a period of 90 days or more, or should they violate any of the provisions of this article or any other applicable city, state, or federal law related to such amusement centers or machines, their license shall be subject to revocation and the same may not be renewed unless and until the applicant for a license meets all provisions of any applicable law, including the above spacing requirements. 
(Ord. No. 950, § X, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-28. - Hours of operation. 
(a)  A game room may operate between the hours of 8:00 a.m.—11:00 p.m. CST from Sunday through Thursday and 8:00 a.m.—11:59 p.m. CST on Friday and Saturday so as to limit the increase of personal crimes such as assaults and robberies. 
(b)  An owner or operator commits a Class C misdemeanor offense if the owner or operator intentionally or knowingly operates a game room in violation of this section punishable by a fine of up to $2,000.00 per violation per day. 
(Ord. No. 950, § XI, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-29. - Game room memberships. 
(a)  A game room owner or operator shall not restrict entry to a game room or prohibit the use of an amusement redemption machine by a patron through the requirement of a game room membership. 
(b)  An owner or operator commits a Class C misdemeanor offense if the owner or operator intentionally or knowingly operates a game room in violation of this subsection punishable by a fine of up to $2,000.00 per violation per day. 
(Ord. No. 950, § XII, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-30. - Term, nontransferable. 
Any license issued pursuant to this article shall be non-transferable for the full period of its effectiveness. 
(Ord. No. 950, § XIII, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-31. - Display. 
A licensed issued pursuant to this article shall at all times be displayed in some conspicuous place within the licensed place of business. 
(Ord. No. 950, § XIV, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-32. - Revocation. 
The power of revocation shall be exercised upon the following grounds only: 
(1)  For the violation of any of the provisions of this article. 
(2)  For knowingly permitting the presence on the premises of a person under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs. 
(3)  For knowingly permitting disorderly conduct or immoral practices on the premises. 
(4)  For knowingly permitting the violation of the laws of the state of this article or any other ordinance of the city. 
(5)  For failure to comply with the regulations of this article relating to minors. 
(Ord. No. 950, § XV, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Sec. 6-33. - Penalty clause. 
Any person who violates any provision of this article for which no other penalty is set forth shall, upon conviction, be subject to a penalty of not more than $2,000.00 per machine, per incident or per day in which such condition exists. Each day that such violation is permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense. The term "person" as used in this section shall include the owner, occupant, mortgager or vendor in possession, assignee or renter, receiver, executor, trustee, or lessee, agent or another person, form or corporation directly, or indirectly, in control of a building or tract of land. 
(Ord. No. 950, § XVI, 3-8-2016; Ord. No. 951, 3-22-2016)  
Chapter 8 - ANIMALS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Health and safety of animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 821.001 et seq.; Type A municipality may regulate animals running at large, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 215.026; rabies control, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.001 et seq.; municipality may adopt rabies control chapter of state law, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.013; municipality may establish local rabies control program, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.015; designation of local rabies control authority, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.017; subchapter of state law does not preempt municipal regulation or prohibition of dangerous wild animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.116(b). 
 
Sec. 8-1. - Definitions. 
Animal means any vertebrate animal other than human beings. 
Animal nuisance means the public nuisance created by an animal or animals within the city limits that affect the quality of life or persons of normal nervous sensibilities, including but not limited to: 
(1)  Excessive noise produced by barking, whining, digging, or any other noise activity. 
(2)  Destruction of public or private property belonging to any person other than the owner. 
(3)  Any foul or noxious odor produced by the offending animal or animals. 
(4)  Allowing the animals to urinate or defecate on any public or private property other than that of the owner unless such waste is removed and properly disposed by the custodian of the animal. 
At large means not physically restrained to the premises of the owner or not under the direct control of the owner, handler, or trainer (direct control shall mean securely confined by leash, chain, or other devise not more than six feet in length held by a person capable of controlling the animal.) 
Cat kennel means any place in which more than three feline animals over three months of age are confined. This definition excludes animal hospitals. 
Dog kennel means any building, structure or enclosure, where three canine animals over the age of three months of age are confined. This definition excludes animal hospitals. 
Dog means any male or female canine. 
Household means those who dwell in the same residence and compose a family. 
Hybrid animal means any offspring of two animals of different species. 
Owner means any person or legal entity owning, harboring, or caring for an animal. 
Provocation means any purposeful act that causes an animal to bite, scratch or otherwise attack in protection of self, owner, or owner's property. 
Restraint or restrained means any physical means of controlling an animal, to include but not limited to cage, fence, leash (or chain) or automobile (in the cab or tied). 
Street line means the nearest edge of any sidewalk, or if there is none, then the nearest edge of any curb, or if there is none, then the nearest edge of the improved portion of the public right-of-way. 
Vicious animal means any animal with the propensity, tendency, or disposition to attack human or domestic animals unprovoked. Any animal that has attacked or attempted to attack humans or domestic animals except when the victim is unlawfully on the premises of the owner. 
Wild animal means an undomesticated animal with the propensity, tendency, or disposition for unprovoked attacks on humans or domestic animals. 
Working day means any day of the week excluding weekends and city observed holidays. 
(Ord. No. 866, § I, 9-13-2011; Ord. No. 956, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 8-2. - Animal control officers and duties. 
(a)  Officers. The positions of the chief animal control officers and deputy animal control officers are hereby established. 
(b)  Department. The animal control department shall function as a department of the city subject to guidelines and procedures adopted by the city council for its operations. 
(c)  Compensation. The chief animal control officer and deputy animal control officer shall receive such compensation as shall be established by the city's annual fiscal budget. The deputy animal control officer is hereby authorized and directed to perform, in conjunction with and under the supervision of the chief animal control officer, the powers and duties herein bestowed upon and required to be performed by said chief animal control officer. 
(d)  Police powers. The animal control officer shall be vested with the necessary police powers for the exclusive purpose of enforcing the provisions of this chapter, and it shall be his duty to issue citations for violations of any of the provisions of this chapter. Both shall enforce all of the laws of the city, county, and state relating to the care, treatment and impounding of animals and to the prevention of cruelty to animals. This exercise of said police powers shall be under the direct supervision of the chief of police or designated representative. 
(e)  Powers to collect fees. The animal control officer shall be vested with the powers to collect fees established by this section, subsection (m) and enforce the provisions of this chapter as described herein. All sums so collected shall be paid over to the finance department promptly as directed. 
(f)  Duties. It is hereby made the duty of the animal control officer to enforce any other sections of this chapter whether as a duty or not. 
(g)  Interference with duty. No person shall rescue or attempt to neither rescue any animal mentioned herein from the possession of any animal control officer nor interfere with the chief animal control officer, or his deputies, in the performance of their official duties. 
(h)  Entering the premises. The animal control officer or any police officer of the city is authorized to enter upon any premises upon which any animal is kept, for the purposes of taking up, seizing or impounding any animal found running at large, or staked, herded or grazing thereon, contrary to provisions of this chapter for the purpose of ascertaining whether such animal is duly vaccinated for the control of rabies as provided in this chapter, or for the purpose of inspecting the premises to ascertain whether any law of the city or state relating to the care, treatment or impounding of animals or the prevention of cruelty to animals is being violated, provided there is probable cause to believe there is a violation. 
(i)  Animal control shelter. There shall be provided by the city a suitable building or enclosure to keep and safely hold all animals herein enumerated which are subject to be impounded, which shall be known and designated as the "animal control shelter". 
(j)  Impounding. It shall be the duty of the animal control officer or any peace officer to take up, impound, or safely keep any animal found to be in violation of this chapter. 
(1)  Animal control officers or other law enforcement officers shall have the power to impound animals which create an animal nuisance for the purpose of abating the nuisance as follows: 
a.  On public property in all cases. 
b.  On private property, if: 
1.  The consent of the property owner or resident is obtained; 
2.  The officer reasonably believes there is immediate or imminent danger or peril to the public if the animal in question is not impounded; 
3.  If the animal or animals are found to be in violation of subsection (h); 
4.  Authorized by appropriate courts of law, or 
5.  If property is vacant of buildings and residents to serve as a custodian for the animal. 
(2)  Animal control officers or other law enforcement officer shall have the power to impound unrestrained animals for the purpose of abating the nuisance as follows: 
a.  On public property in all cases; 
b.  On private property with the consent of the property owner or resident; 
c.  On private property when in pursuit of an animal, which he believes, is subject to impoundment under the provisions of this chapter; 
d.  When authorized by an appropriate court of law; 
e.  On private if property is vacant of buildings and residents to serve as a custodian for the animal. 
(k)  Care of animal. It shall be the duty of the animal control officer to provide impounded animals with adequate food, water, and shelter for the period of their impoundment. 
(l)  Reclaiming. The animal control officer shall make every attempt within reason to notify the owner of an animal, at his last known residence, immediately after impounding either by mail, telephone, or personal contact. The owner of an impounded animal may reclaim said animal at any time prior to final disposition of said animal upon payment of all charges incurred by said impoundment. 
(m)  Fees. The animal control officer shall charge, and collect the following fees for services and impounding animals. 
(1)  Dogs and cats: $25.00 for impounding plus $10.00 per day board. 
(2)  Rabies vaccination (vaccination or proof of current vaccination is required prior to release of any dog or cat): Charge based on veterinarians fee plus $5.00 for transportation of animal. 
(3)  Livestock: $75.00 for impounding plus $25.00 per day board. 
(4)  Other fees: 
a.  Euthanizations dogs and cats: $10.00. 
b.  Trap use deposit: There shall be paid to the city a refundable $15.00 deposit for each trap issued by the animal control officer which shall be refundable upon their return in like conditions as when issued. 
(5)  Payment of any applicable fees is due in advance of the animal's release to owner or claimant. 
(6)  Any person surrendering a pet for any reason shall be assessed a fee of $40.00. 
(n)  Accounting for sums collected. The animal control officer shall pay over to the finance director all sums collected by him, pursuant to the terms of this chapter, promptly as directed. 
(o)  Revenue allocation. All sums received by the city pursuant to the terms of this chapter shall be deposited into the city's general fund. 
(p)  Destruction of impounded animals unfit for use by age, crippled, diseased, or wild. It shall be the duty of the animal control officers to order the destruction of any animal lawfully taken into custody, which in the opinion of the animal control officer is, by reason of old age, unfit for use, or which is infected with a dangerous or communicable disease, or which is in an incurably crippled condition, or which is adjudged by a report of a licensed veterinarian to be afflicted with any painful, incurable disease. A reasonable attempt shall be made to notify the owner (if known) prior to taking action, however the humane destruction of a sick or injured animal may necessitate immediate action. 
(q)  Disposition of vicious animals. 
(1)  The chief of police, or his designee, may order the seizure and humane euthanization of any vicious animal found within the corporate limits of the city. 
(2)  The chief of police, or his designee may order that a vicious animal be: 
a.  Permanently removed from the corporate limits of the city; 
b.  Transferred permanently to an appropriate animal care facility; or 
c.  Euthanized in the event that an animal is found in violation of any order described in subsection a. or b. above. 
(Ord. No. 866, § II, 9-13-2011; Ord. No. 956, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 8-3. - Dogs and cats. 
(a)  Tags must be shown. No person shall fail or refuse to show the animal control officer or any police officer of said city, the rabies vaccination tag for any duly vaccinated dog or cat kept or remaining within any home or upon any enclosed premises under his immediate control. Said vaccination tag shall be attached to a neck collar and be worn by the animal at all times. If a tag is lost it shall be the responsibility of the owner to replace the tag as soon as possible in order to return to compliance of this section. 
(b)  Removal of vaccination tags. No unauthorized person shall remove from any dog or cat any collar, harness, or other devise to which is attached a vaccination tag for the current year, or to remove such tag there from. 
(c)  Counterfeiting tags. No person shall imitate or counterfeit the tags in this section provided for, or shall use any imitation or counterfeit of such tag. 
(d)  Dogs running at large prohibited. No person owning, harboring, or caring for a dog shall allow said animal to be off the premises of its owner unless securely confined by a strong leash not to exceed six feet in length continuously held by a person capable of controlling the dog or confined to an automobile. 
(e)  Impounding. It shall be the duty of the animal control officer and of any police officer of said city, to take up all dogs found in violation hereof. When such dog is taken up by a police officer, it shall be delivered by him to the animal control officer. All such dogs shall be impounded in the city's animal control shelter. 
(f)  Rabies vaccination required. Every person owning or harboring a dog or cat in the city shall cause such dog or cat to be vaccinated for rabies with an approved rabies vaccine: 
(1)  Immediately upon it's procurement if it is over four months old and has not been so vaccinated within a period of one year prior to the procurement of said animal, or 
(2)  As soon as possible after the dog or cat has attained the age of three months, provided, however, that such vaccination has been accomplished by the time it attains the age of four months. 
(g)  Annual vaccination required. Every person owning or harboring in the city a dog or cat which has been vaccinated with an approved vaccine shall cause the dog or cat to be revaccinated within a period not to exceed one year. 
(h)  Rabies certificate. Every person keeping, harboring or having in the city any dog or cat required by this section to be vaccinated shall at all times while such dog or cat is thus kept, harbored or had, have in his possession a certificate issued by a person licensed by the state or any other state or nation to practice veterinary medicine, which certificate shall specify that such dog or cat has been vaccinated in accordance with provisions of this section. At the time a dog or cat is vaccinated, a vaccination tag shall be stamped with the date of vaccination and the type of vaccine used. 
(i)  Rabies vaccination evidence. At the time a dog or cat is vaccinated, a vaccination tag shall be stamped with the date of vaccination and the type of vaccine used. It is the pet owner's responsibility to keep in his/her possession the certificate issued to them at the time of the animal's vaccination and to produce said certificate if requested by the animal control officer or police officer. 
(j)  Rabies precautions. Officers or persons capturing dogs or cats suspected of having rabies under the provisions of this section shall separately confine such dog or cat, shall report the capture to a licensed veterinarian, and shall submit said animal to the examination of a veterinarian. It shall be the duty of the veterinarian to ascertain whether or not the dog or cat is infected with rabies. Such dog or cat shall not be killed, but shall be kept in confinement until further observation of such dog or cat claimed by its owner is not necessary for the determination of the presence or the absence of rabies. Stray or unclaimed animals shall be processed as allowed by state health regulations incurring the least expense upon the residents of the city. 
(k)  Unlawful for any person to fail to notify the city's police department or animal control officer regarding rabid dog. It shall be unlawful for any person having knowledge of the whereabouts of an animal known to have or suspected of having rabies or has shown symptoms of rabies to fail, refuse or neglect to allow the city's police department or animal control officer, to make an inspection or examination that such animal has or does not have rabies. The city's police department or animal control officer shall likewise be notified of any person bitten by an animal of a species subject to rabies, whether or not the animal is suspected of having rabies. 
(l)  Ten-day quarantine. 
(1)  Whenever it is shown that any dog, cat, or other animal without proof of current rabies vaccination has bitten any person, no person owning or harboring said animal, upon order of the animal control officer or any police officer, shall fail, refuse, neglect to take or cause to be promptly taken, such animal to a veterinarian to be held in quarantine for a period of ten days. Such animal may not be released from quarantine without the authorization of the veterinarian in charge. The total cost of the confinement for a ten-day period shall be borne by the owner. 
(2)  The owner of a duly vaccinated animal that has bitten or scratched a person, causing skin abrasion, will assume personal responsibility for the quarantine of said animal for the ten days only under the following circumstances: 
a.  The facilities must be sufficiently secure so as to prevent the escape of said animal to prevent contact of said animal with any person other than the immediate family of the owner. 
b.  The facilities are inspected and approved by the animal control officer. 
c.  The animal is examined by a licensed veterinarian at least on the first day of quarantine period and the last day of the quarantine period. 
d.  If the animal shall become ill or dies suddenly the animal control officer shall be notified immediately and shall conduct an on-site visual inspection of the animal. 
e.  Release from quarantine may be accomplished only by written authorization by the inspecting veterinarian. 
(3)  If an animal is believed to have rabies or has been bitten by an animal suspected of having rabies, such animal shall, upon order of the animal control officer either is quarantined by a licensed veterinarian for the appropriate period of time or humanely euthanized. If human exposure to such an animal has occurred, the head of such animal shall be removed and submitted to the state department of health lab for rabies diagnosis. 
(4)  The violation of the observation confinement of the biting animal as provided in subsection (2) shall be just cause for seizure and confinement of the animal at a licensed veterinary facility. 
(5)  No wild animals will be placed in quarantine. All wild animals involved in biting incidents will be humanely euthanized in such a manner that the brain is not mutilated. The brain shall be submitted to a state department of health lab for rabies diagnosis. 
(6)  The total cost of the confinement period shall be borne by the owner or the animal with the following exception: 
If it can be proved that such a bite or scratch was caused by a provocation, the person responsible for said provocation shall bear the expense of any quarantine, provided however, that the animal in question was not in violation of any provision of this section at the time of the attack. 
(m)  Knowledge of bite; duty of report. If any animal within the corporate limits of the city shall bite or scratch any person or so injure any person so as to cause a skin abrasion, and such facts be known to the owner of such animal, such owner shall immediately give his name and address together with the animal's license tag number to the person bitten or injured, provided, however that the person so bitten or injured is over 18 years of age. If the person bitten or injured is under the age of 18 years then such required information shall be given to a parent or guardian. In addition thereto, the owner of such animal shall immediately thereafter, and in no event later than 24 hours thereafter, notify the police department or animal control officer giving his name, animal's vaccination tag number, the name of the victim, and any other information that the police department or animal control officer may require. 
(n)  Application for returning impounded animal. Subject to the other provisions of this section, any person may make application to the animal control officer for the return of any dog, cat, or other animal, and upon presentation of proof satisfactory to said animal control officer that such person is the owner or is rightfully entitled to the possession of such animal, may recover the same upon payment of any required fee including a fee for rabies vaccination if such is not current. If an animal so impounded is not current for rabies vaccination, the animal control officer shall take said animal to a licensed veterinarian for rabies vaccination prior to release to its owner. 
(o)  Period of impounding and final disposition. The city encourages and supports development of "pet adoption" programs by organizations within the community, and will cooperatively work with such organizations to encourage responsible pet adoption. 
(1)  Dogs and cats—Three working days. 
(2)  Dogs and cats shall be kept for two working days following the minimum period of impoundment for possible sale to the public, or transfer to a pet adoption program. 
(p)  Maximum number of animals. 
(1)  No household shall keep or harbor more than four dogs or four cats or a combination of dogs and cats not to exceed four in the corporate limits of the city except temporarily while any of the dogs or cats hereto allowed is nursing a litter of puppies or kittens until said litter attains the age of three months at which time the household must return to compliance of this section. The provisions of animal nuisance, as hereto defined, shall apply during this exemption. 
(2)  No boarding kennel shall be allowed within the city except exempted animal hospitals. 
(Ord. No. 866, § III, 9-13-2011; Ord. No. 956, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 8-4. - Other animals. 
(a)  Animals not allowed within the city. It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and no person shall keep or maintain at their residence any of the following animals within the city. 
(1)  Horse, colt, jack or mule; 
(2)  Goats or sheep; 
(3)  Cattle including ox, steer, bull, cow or calf; 
(4)  Pigs or hogs; and 
(5)  Bees, or hive of bees. 
(6)  Monkeys. 
(b)  Maximum number of fowls and rabbits. It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and no person shall keep or maintain at their residence a cumulative total exceeding ten chickens, geese, ducks, turkeys, pheasants, doves, pigeons, squabs, roosters, similar fowl, or rabbits within the city. An adult rooster (crowing age) may be substituted for one of the ten fowl allowed as per subsection (c) of this section. 
(c)  Fowls and rabbits not to run at large. It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and no person shall allow fowls or rabbits to run or fly at large or go upon the premises of any other person, or upon a public way in the city. Said animals shall be kept in a confined area no closer than 30 feet to the nearest street line, or 20 feet to the nearest property line. 
(d)  Sale of rabbit or fowl. Nothing in this section shall prohibit the display or sale of any rabbit or fowl by any dealer, hatchery, or store engaged in the business of selling the same to be raised for food purposes whenever such dealer, hatchery, or store has proper facilities for the display and care of such animals or fowl and is in compliance with city zoning regulations. 
(e)  Advertisement, sale, and redemption fee for impounded livestock. After giving five days notice in the newspaper, the animal control officer may sell at public stockyards any impounded animal covered by ordinance. Redemption by the owner or his agent is possible any time prior to sale by paying $75.00 impounding fee plus $15.00 per day board. In the case of redemption, all advertising fees shall be paid by the owner. All moneys so received by virtue of sale of such animals shall be turned over to the city's finance director for deposit into the city's general fund. 
(f)  Disposition of animals. Any animal covered under this section not sold or redeemed may be disposed of by the animal control officer or police chief in whatever manner is in the best interest of the city. 
(Ord. No. 866, § IV, 9-13-2011; Ord. No. 956, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 8-5. - Wild animals. 
(a)  Certain animals prohibited. It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and no person or business shall keep or maintain in the city any wild or vicious animal or reptile of any nature whatsoever, including hybrid animals. 
(b)  Carnivals or circuses. Nothing in this section shall be construed to apply to the temporary display of wild or vicious animals or reptiles in carnivals, zoos, museums, exhibitions, or circuses provided that prior city council approval has been obtained for such a display and inspected by the animal control officer and that such animals or reptiles are so restricted so as to pose no threat to the public safety and provided further that such animals so displayed will be well cared for, free from disease and kept in sanitary conditions. 
(c)  Exception for transportation of animals through city. The requirements of this section shall not be applicable to persons transporting wild or vicious animals through the city providing that the transporter has taken adequate safeguards to protect the public and does not park the transporting vehicle within the city limits of the city. 
(Ord. No. 866, § V, 9-13-2011; Ord. No. 956, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 8-6. - Miscellaneous rules. 
(a)  Carcass of animal. It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and no person shall cause, suffer or permit the carcass of any animal to remain upon any lot, premises or place owned, controlled or occupied by him or it for a period of more than 24 hours. 
(b)  Manure bins and removal of manure. Every person owning or occupying premises where manure from any pigeon, fowl, rabbit or other animal accumulates shall provide for the removal of such manure daily, boxes, bins or receptacles of a design and construction acceptable to the animal control officer shall be provided by the owner or occupant of such premises, and such boxes, bins or receptacles shall be used only for the purpose of containing the accumulation of manure, which shall be placed therein or removed there from, and in no instance shall manure be so placed in such boxes or receptacles in such a manner as to prevent the tight closing of the lid; provided, however, that nothing contained herein shall apply to manure which is spread as fertilizer over or around cultivated plants, vines, vegetables, lawns, bushes or trees, or to manure kept by any nursery for commercial fertilizer purposes, unless such manure creates a nuisance either from fly breeding or excessive obnoxious odors. Said boxes, bins or receptacles shall be constructed of brick, stone, concrete, metal or wood lines with metal or other sound material, and shall be proof against access to the contents thereof by files. The contents of said boxes, bins, or receptacles shall be removed once a week. 
(c)  Animal control officer may order premises and manure bins cleaned and disinfected. No person who is ordered by the animal control officer to clean or disinfect any stables, bar, corral, stall, pen, coop, building, or place in which any fowl, bird or other animal kept, or who is ordered by such officer to clean or disinfect any box, bin or receptacle used for the accumulation of manure shall fail, neglect to clean or disinfect such stable, bar, corral, stall, pen, coop, building place, box, bin, or receptacle. 
(d)  Animals prohibited in certain areas. No person shall allow any animal into an area where food is prepared for commercial purposes with the exception of dogs aiding the seeing or hearing impaired. 
(e)  Fee a debt. The amount of any fee imposed by this section shall be defined a debt to the city and any person keeping any animal without having complied with the provisions of this section shall be liable to an action in the name of the city in any court of competent jurisdiction for the amount of the fees or penalties imposed and required by this section to be paid for the privilege of keeping such animal and it shall be the duty of the animal control officer to cause a civil complaint to be filed against any person violating any of the provisions of this section, and the city chief of police shall cause an action to be brought against any person failing to pay penalty required by the provisions of this section for the recovery of the same. 
(f)  Keeping diseased animals prohibited; exception. No person except a licensed veterinarian shall keep any animal which is known or believed by him to be infected with any dangerous or communicable disease, or which is afflicted with any painful disease believed by him to be incurable, without written permission to do so from an animal control officer of the city. 
(g)  Rabies. Whenever it is suspected that any animal shall have contracted rabies, or shall have been bitten by another animal having, or suspected of having rabies, the animal control officer, or police officers will be immediately notified and subsection 8-3(j) shall apply. 
(h)  Penalties. A person who shall be found guilty of violating this chapter may be assessed a fine of not more than $1,000.00. Each day the violation occurs may be deemed a separate offense. Repeat offenses may be punished by no less than $200.00 nor more than $1,000.00. 
(i)  Applicability of chapter. Whenever any reference is made to any portion of this chapter such reference applies to all amendments and additions thereto now or hereafter made. The present tense includes the past and future tense and the future, the present. Whenever a power is granted to, or a duty imposed upon, the animal control officer and other public officers, the power may be exercised or the duty may be performed by a deputy of the officers or by a person authorized, pursuant to law, by the officer, unless this chapter expressly provides otherwise. 
(j)  Unlawful to rescue animals. It shall be unlawful to rescue or turn loose any animal impounded by the city by whatever method. 
(k)  Reclamation and prosecution. The owner of any animal impounded remains subject to prosecution for violation of this chapter regardless of whether or not such animal is reclaimed. Such owner shall remain liable for all fees incurred by said animal regardless of whether or not the animal is reclaimed. 
(l)  Chemicals/traps prohibited. The use of cyanic pallet traps or any other kind of trap containing a substance noxious to man is prohibited within the city limits, unless deemed necessary by the Texas Department of Health for the control of communicable disease. 
(m)  Inhumane traps prohibited. No person shall set up or allow to be set up on his property within the city limits any kind of trap that tears, cuts, or in any way mutilates the prey. This will not apply to traps used to catch common rodents, i.e., rats, mice, gophers, and ground squirrels. Such traps may be used on the order of the animal control officer for the control of communicable diseases. 
(n)  Tin traps prohibited. Tin traps are not to be allowed in the city limits unless ordered by the animal control officer. 
(Ord. No. 866, § VI, 9-13-2011; Ord. No. 956, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 8-7. - Dogs running at large. 
(a)  No dog, licensed or not, shall be allowed to run at large or upon the premises of anyone other than the owner. If any such dog is found running at large in violation of this section, and the owner is unknown the dog shall be taken up and impounded. 
(b)  If a dog is found running at large in violation of this section and the owner is known, the dog will be taken to the owner and the owner may be issued a citation for failure to keep his dog from running at large, or the dog may be taken up and impounded. 
(c)  If a dog is found running at large in violation of this section and the owner is unknown and the dog cannot be safely taken up and impounded, such dog may be tranquilized and taken up and impounded, or when such dog be deemed vicious or dangerous to persons or other animals and cannot be tranquilized, the dog may be humanely euthanized by a police officer or under the supervision of a police officer. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 3, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-8. - Muzzling vicious cats and dogs. 
The animal control officer may order a vicious cat or dog to be kept muzzled, or that such cat or dog may be kept within a sufficient enclosure. Failure to keep such animal muzzled or within a sufficient enclosure, is deemed a violation of this Code. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 4, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-9. - Abandonment and neglect. 
No person who has within his control, either temporarily or permanently, any cat or dog, shall abandon the same in the city, nor shall any person allow any cat or dog to be left without proper food, water, and shelter within the city. Failure by an owner to redeem an impounded cat or dog within three days constitutes abandonment. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 5, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-10. - Proclamation ordering muzzling of cats or dogs; destruction of rabies suspect cat or dog. 
(a)  Whenever it becomes necessary to safeguard the public from the dangers of rabies, the mayor, if he deems it necessary, shall issue a proclamation ordering every person owning or keeping a cat or dog to confine it securely on his premises unless such cat or dog has a muzzle of sufficient strength to prevent its biting any person. 
(b)  All cats and dogs which are noticeably affected with rabies and displaying vicious propensities may be killed under the supervision of any police officer without notice of the owner. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 6, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-11. - Rabies control measures report; quarantine and disposition of rabies or rabies suspect animals. 
(a)  When a cat or dog has been bitten by an animal known to have rabies, the cat or dog shall be quarantined for a period of 180 days at a veterinary facility or destroyed by a veterinarian at the discretion of the owner and at the owner's expense. 
(b)  When a dog or cat has been bitten by an animal suspected of having rabies, and the rabies suspect animal is captured and quarantined at a veterinary facility, the animal bitten will also be quarantined for ten days. Disposition of both animals will be determined by the veterinarian having custody of each of the animals. 
(c)  Animal owners shall notify the city animal control officer of the fact that his cat or dog has been exposed to rabies and, at his discretion, the animal control officer is empowered to have such cat or dog removed from the owner's premises to a veterinary facility for observation at the owner's expense. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any person knowing or suspecting a cat or dog to have rabies to dispose of such cat or dog without written permission of the city animal control officer. 
(e)  Every owner or other person, upon ascertaining that a cat or dog is rabies, shall immediately notify the animal control officer who shall either remove the cat or dog to the animal shelter, if possible, and if not, to summarily have it destroyed. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 7, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-12. - Physician's report of animal bites. 
It shall be the duty of every physician or other practitioner to report to the city police department the names and addresses of persons treated for bites inflicted by animals together with such information necessary to assist the investigation of the bite accident. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 8, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-13. - Refusing to cooperate and/or interfering with impounding of cat or dog. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse to deliver any unlicensed or unvaccinated cat or dog upon demand for impounding, or to interfere with an attempt to prevent the animal control officer or any of his deputies, animal wardens or any city police officer from catching or impounding any cat or dog running at large. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. II, § 10, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-14. - Duty of officers. 
It shall be the duty of the animal control officer, any of his deputies, animal warden or any police officer to pick up and impound, subject to the provisions of this chapter, all animals that are in violation of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 1, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-15. - Authority to enter. 
The animal control officer, his deputy, animal warden or any city police officer, while on duty, is hereby authorized to enter upon any public place, unfenced private property, lot, tract or parcel of land that is not the land of the owner of the animal within the city, whether in the immediate presence of the owner or custodian or otherwise, for the purpose of seizing or impounding any animal running at large thereon. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 2, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-16. - Impoundment records. 
Records of all impounded animals will be kept in accordance with the administrative procedures approved by the city manager. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 3, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-17. - Disposition of cats and dogs—Period of keeping. 
All cats and dogs not claimed and released within 72 hours after being impounded shall be destroyed or otherwise disposed of as the city council may so designate. In the case of a sick, injured, diseased or infected animal, the animal control officer or a veterinarian may waive the 72-hour waiting period, when in his professional opinion it would be dangerous, inhumane or likely to cause the spread of the disease to hold such animal for such period. The person allowing the animal to get into such poor, sick, diseased or injured condition is hereby held responsible for such condition and the animal control officer and/or the veterinarian is hereby relieved of responsibility in destroying the animal. In the case of a well-kept animal, with or without collar or harness and license tag, the animal control officer will continue impoundment of the animal for an additional 24 hours to allow additional time for redemption and a call to the city secretary for any special report of lost animal; however, the final responsibility for location of an impounded animal is that of the owner. The animal control officer shall notify his supervisor of the extended impoundment and thereafter may destroy or otherwise dispose of the animal and both the animal control officer and the supervisor are hereby relieved of responsibility in destroying the animal. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 4, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-18. - Disposition of cats and dogs—Sale authorization. 
At any time after the period of time for redemption of impounded cats or dogs shall have expired the animal control officer may, without further notice and without advertising in any manner, sell at private sale or public auction for cash any cat or dog not redeemed or reclaimed. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 5, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-19. - Disposition of cats and dogs—Other. 
All impounded dogs or cats that remain unredeemed, unclaimed or unsold after the period of time for redemption has expired, shall forthwith be disposed of by the animal control officer according to current policies. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 6, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-20. - Disposition of cats and dogs—Release in case of willful release of dogs and cats. 
Whenever the city manager is satisfied that any cat or dog has been willfully released from any enclosure by any person other than the owner with the intention of having the same impounded to injure the owner thereof, he shall order the animal control officer to release the cat or dog so impounded without any city impoundment fee or cost to the owner. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 7, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-21. - Disposition of cats and dogs—Redemption of cats and dogs; procedure, fees. 
(a)  The owner of any licensed cat or dog may redeem such cat or dog at any time prior to sale or adoption, by the payment of impounding fee of $10.00 and fee per day of $2.00 plus any medical or other cost expended on behalf of subject animal. 
(b)  The impounding and boarding fee shall be doubled for any owned cat or dog impounded for a second time within a one-year period. A warning notice shall be issued to the owner stating that if a third offense occurs with a one-year time period of the second offense, a summons shall be issued. 
(c)  Owners reclaiming such cat or dog for a third time or thereafter, shall be charged impounding and boarding fees in accordance with the amount designated in the second offense, and issued a municipal court summons for violation of this chapter. 
(d)  The owner of any impounded unlicensed cat or dog may redeem such cat or dog any time prior to sale or disposition by having such cat or dog duly licensed, and paying the impounding fee and fee per day for each day such cat or dog shall have been impounded, plus any medical or other costs expended on behalf of subject animal. License and vaccination requirements are not applicable if the animal is not going to be housed in this city. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 8, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-22. - Disposition of cats and dogs—Proceeds. 
The money collected shall be deposited in accordance with current directives, credited toward and used solely for the expense of the animal control shelter operation. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 9, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-23. - Breaking and entering animal control shelter, releasing, injuring confined animals. 
It shall be unlawful for any unauthorized person to forcibly open the gate or otherwise enter the animal control shelter, in any way damage the animal control shelter, injure animals therein, or to release, drive out or turn loose therefrom or to permit the escape of any animal therein confined. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. III, § 10, 8-12-1986)  
Sec. 8-24. - Penalty. 
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not exceeding $200.00, and each and every day of such violation shall be deemed a separate and complete offense. 
(Ord. No. 532, div. IV, § 2, 8-12-1986)  
Chapter 10 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Municipal regulation of housing and other structures, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001 et seq.; International Residential Code as municipal residential building code, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.212; International Building Code as municipal commercial building code, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.216; national electrical code applicable statewide for construction, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.214; municipal authority concerning swimming pool enclosures, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.101; standards for public pools and spas, 25 Tex. Admin. Code § 265.181 et seq.; municipal authority concerning plumbing and house draining, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.012; municipal authority concerning substandard building, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001; additional authority to secure substandard building, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 214.0011, 214.0015; time for issuance of municipal building permit, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.904; verification of builder registration with state, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.906. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 10-1. - Trench safety. 
On all construction projects, public or private, within the boundaries of the city, or within the extraterritorial jurisdiction, the bid document and the contract shall contain: 
(1)  Detailed plans and specifications for adequate safety systems that meet OSHA standards; and 
(2)  A pay item for those safety systems. This requirement shall not apply to persons subject to safety standards adopted under state law. 
Violation of OSHA witnessed by the building inspectors in the field should be reported to OSHA and the construction job superintendent. 
(Ord. No. 554, §§ I, II, 3-8-1988)  
Sec. 10-2. - Registration and proof of state-issued license requirement. 
Company registration with the city is required prior to issuance of any mechanical permit. Proof of current state-issued license must be presented annually. 
(Ord. No. 753, § 3, 9-16-2004)  
Secs. 10-3—10-22. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - SUBSTANDARD BUILDINGS 
 
Sec. 10-23. - Intent, purpose of article. 
(a)  Name. This article shall be commonly referred to as the city's "Substandard Building Ordinance." 
(b)  Purpose. This article is adopted so that the city council may promote the public health, safety, and general welfare within the city through the regulation of substandard and dangerous buildings or structures. By requiring the repair and/or demolition of substandard and dangerous buildings and structures, the city council seeks to protect property values and prevent bodily injury, death, and property damage within the city limits. 
(c)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Appraised value means the value given the structure by the county tax assessor's office. 
Building means any structure of any kind or any part thereof, erected for the support, shelter or enclosure of persons, animals, chattel or property of any kind. 
Building inspector means the person appointed by the city to conduct periodic inspections of buildings and structures to ensure that the same are being maintained in a manner consistent with prescribed building codes of the city and not in violation of this article. 
Diligent effort means the best or a reasonable effort to determine the identity and address of an owner, a lienholder, or a mortgagee including a search of the following records: 
(1)  County real property records of the county in which the building is located; 
(2)  Appraisal district records of the appraisal district in which the building is located; 
(3)  Records of the secretary of state; 
(4)  Assumed name records of the county in which the building is located; 
(5)  City tax records; and 
(6)  City utility records. 
Minimum housing standards means those standards adopted by the city, including, if applicable, building, electrical, plumbing, gas, mechanical, existing building and fire prevention codes and any other housing and structure regulations adopted under V.T.C.A., Local Government Code chapter 214. 
Owner means any person, agent, firm, corporation, or other entity named in the real property records of the county where the building is located as owning the property. 
Structure means that which is built or constructed, an edifice or building of any kind, or any piece of work artificially built or composed of parts joined together in some definite manner, or any part thereof. 
(Ord. No. 891, § I, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-24. - Declaration of nuisance. 
Any building or structure requiring repair, removal or demolition, as described and defined herein, and all buildings or structures within the city which are unsafe, unsanitary or otherwise dangerous to the health, safety and general welfare of the citizens of the city are hereby declared to be a public nuisance and unlawful and subject to the provisions of this article regarding repair, removal or demolition. 
(Ord. No. 891, § II, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-25. - Inspection. 
An inspection shall be made of every building located within the city which is suspected of being in violation of this article. The building inspector, or his official designee, is hereby authorized to conduct inspections of buildings suspected of being in violation of this article and take such actions as may be required to enforce the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 891, § III, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-26. - Notice of violation. 
(a)  Whenever a violation of this article has been discovered and reported by the building inspector, or his designee, a public hearing shall be held by the city council to determine whether a building complies with the standards set out in this article. 
(b)  A notice of the hearing shall be sent to the occupant, if any, and record owner, lienholder or mortgagee. Such notice shall be in writing and shall be served by personal delivery or by certified mail return receipt requested. Additionally, a copy of the notice shall be posted on the front door of each affected structure situated on the property or as close to the front door as practicable. It is not necessary that the notice to the occupant of the property list an occupant by name. Service of the notice may be accomplished by the first class U.S. mail or by personal delivery to any occupant of the property who is above 18 years of age. 
(c)  The notice shall contain: 
(1)  The names of all persons to whom notice is being served; 
(2)  The street address or legal description of the premises; 
(3)  The date of inspection; 
(4)  The nature of the violation; 
(5)  The date, time and location of the hearing; and 
(6)  A statement that the owner, lienholder, or mortgagee will be required to submit at the hearing proof of the scope of any work that may be required to comply with the article and the time it will take to reasonably perform the work. 
(Ord. No. 891, § IV, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-27. - Standards. 
The following standards shall be utilized in determining whether a building should be ordered repaired, removed or demolished: 
(1)  The building or structure is liable to partially or fully collapse. 
(2)  The building or structure was constructed or maintained in violation of any provision of the city's building code, or any other applicable ordinance or law of the city, county, state, or federal government. 
(3)  Any wall or other vertical structural members list, lean or buckle to such an extent that a plumb line passing through the center of gravity falls outside of the middle one-third of its base. 
(4)  The foundation or the vertical or horizontal supporting members are 25 percent or more damaged or deteriorated. 
(5)  The nonsupporting coverings of walls, ceilings, roofs, or floors are 50 percent or more damaged or deteriorated. 
(6)  The structure has improperly distributed loads upon the structural members, or the structural members have insufficient strength to be reasonably safe for the purpose used. 
(7)  The structure of any part thereof has been damaged by fire, water, earthquake, wind, vandalism, or other cause to such an extent that it has become dangerous to the public, health, safety and welfare. 
(8)  The structure does not have adequate light, ventilation, or sanitation facilities as required by the city. 
(9)  The structure has inadequate facilities for egress in case of fire or other emergency or has insufficient stairways, elevators, fire escapes or other means of ingress or egress. 
(10)  The structure, because of its condition, is unsafe, unsanitary, or dangerous to the health, safety or general welfare of the city's citizens including all conditions conducive to the harboring of rats or mice or other disease carrying animals or insects reasonably calculated to spread disease. 
(Ord. No. 891, § V, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-28. - Hearings. 
(a)  The date of the hearing shall not be less than ten days after notice is made (as described in section 10-26). 
(b)  If a building is found to be in violation of this article, the city shall require the owner, lienholder, or mortgagee of the building to repair, remove or demolish the building within 30 days, unless it is proven at the hearing that the work cannot reasonably be done in 30 days. 
(c)  If the city allows more than 30 days for the building to be repaired, removed or demolished, the city shall establish specific time schedules for the work to be commenced and performed and shall require the owner, lienholder, or mortgagee to secure the property in a reasonable manner from unauthorized entry while the work is being performed, as determined by the hearing official. 
(d)  The city shall not allow the owner, lienholder or mortgagee more than 90 days to repair, remove or demolish the building or fully perform all worked required to comply with the order unless a detailed plan and time scheduled for the work are submitted at the hearing and it is proven at the hearing that the work cannot reasonably be completed within 90 days because of the scope and complexity of the work. Additionally, the owner, lienholder, or mortgagee must submit work progress reports to demonstrate compliance with the time schedule established. 
(e)  In any case where repairs are estimated to cost 50 percent or more of the appraised value, a building shall be demolished or removed, and in all cases where a structure cannot be repaired so that it will no longer exist in violation of the provisions of this article, it shall be demolished or removed. 
(Ord. No. 891, § VI, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-29. - Order for repair or demolition. 
(a)  After the public hearing, if a building is found to be in violation of the standards set out in this article, the city may order that the building be repaired, removed or demolished within a reasonable time, as established under section 10-28. 
(b)  If the building is ordered to be repaired, removed or demolished, the city shall promptly mail by certified mail, return receipt requested, or personally deliver a copy of the order to the owner of the building and to any lienholder or mortgagee of the building. The city shall make a diligent effort to discover each owner, mortgagee and lienholder having an interest in the building or property on which the building is located. 
(c)  If the ordered action is demolition of the building or structure, demolition shall not occur until a magistrate has issued a seizure and demolition warrant supported by a probable cause affidavit stating that: 
(1)  The building or structure constitute a nuisance; 
(2)  The city has complied with the procedures set forth in this article; 
(3)  Demolition has been ordered by the city; and 
(4)  The time for appeal of the order to district court has expired and no appeal has been taken or, in the alternative, the order was appealed to district court but the appeal has been finally resolved in a manner that does not prevent the city from proceeding with demolition. 
(Ord. No. 891, § VII, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-30. - Notice of repair or demolition. 
(a)  In addition to the order, each identified mortgagee or lienholder shall be sent a notice containing: 
(1)  An identification of the building and property on which it is located (this does not have to be a legal description); 
(2)  A description of the violation of the article; and 
(3)  A statement that the city may demolish the building if the ordered action is not taken. 
(b)  If the notice is returned "refused" or "unclaimed," the validity of the notice is not affected and the notice shall be deemed delivered. 
(c)  Within ten days after the date that the order is issued, the city shall: 
(1)  File a copy of the order in the office of the city secretary; and 
(2)  Publish a notice in a newspaper of general circulation in the city (and where the building is located) stating: 
a.  The street address or legal description of the property; 
b.  The date of the hearing; 
c.  A brief statement indicating the results of the order; and 
d.  Instructions as to where a complete copy of the order may be obtained. 
(Ord. No. 891, § VIII, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-31. - Appeal. 
The owner, lienholder, or mortgagee shall have the right to appeal the decision made at the hearing to a district court. A notice of appeal must be filed with the district court within 30 calendar days from the date the order is mailed to the owner, lienholder or mortgagee, as provided herein. 
(Ord. No. 891, § IX, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-32. - Demolition and repair expenses. 
(a)  Whenever it is discovered upon reinspection that the owner, mortgagee or lienholder has failed to repair, remove or demolish the building or take other ordered action within the allotted time, the city, or its authorized agent, shall make a diligent effort to discover each mortgagee and lienholder having an interest in the building or in the property which the building is located and shall personally deliver or send by certified mail, return receipt requested, to each a notice containing: 
(1)  An identification of the building and property on which it is located (this does not have to be a legal description); 
(2)  A description of the violation of the article; and 
(3)  A statement that the municipality will remove or demolish the building if the ordered action is not taken. 
(b)  Whenever it is discovered upon reinspection that the owner, mortgagee or lienholder has failed to repair, remove or demolish the building or take other ordered action within the allotted time, the city, or its authorized agent, may repair, remove or demolish and remove said building or cause the same to be done and charge the expenses incurred in doing such work or having the same done to the owner, mortgagee or lienholder of said land or otherwise assess the expenses against the property on which the building is located. 
(c)  If such work is done at the expense of the city, then the said expense shall be assessed against any salvage resulting from the demolition of the building and against the lot, tract, or parcel of land, or the premises upon which such expense was incurred. 
(d)  For the purposes of this section, any repair, alteration or improvement made to a building by the city will only be to the extent necessary to bring the building into compliance with the minimum housing standards and only if the building is a residential building with ten or fewer dwelling units; provided, however, the city may elect to obtain a judicial determination by a decree of a court of competent jurisdiction of the existence, in fact, of a public nuisance in cases contemplated by this article. Such judicial determination may include any available remedy for the abatement of such a nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 891, § X, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-33. - Assessment of lien. 
(a)  When the city incurs expenses to repair, remove or demolish a building, the city may assess the expenses on and obtain a lien against the property on which the building is located, unless it is a homestead as protected by the state constitution. The lien arises and attaches to the property when the city has the lien recorded and indexed with the county clerk of the county in which the property is located. The notice shall contain: 
(1)  The name and address of the owner, if that information can be determined with a reasonable effort; 
(2)  A legal description of the real property on which the building was located; 
(3)  The amount of expense incurred by the city; 
(4)  The balance due; and 
(5)  The date on which said work was done or improvements made. 
(b)  The city shall have a privileged lien on such lot or other premises or real estate upon which said building was located, to secure the expenditure so made, second only to other liens as provided by law. It is further provided that for any such expenditure suit may be instituted and foreclosure of said lien may be made in the name of the city; and the statement of expenses so made, as aforesaid, or a certified copy thereof, shall be prima facie proof of the amount expended for such work or expense. 
(c)  The lien is extinguished if the property owner or another person having an interest in the legal title to the property reimburses the city for the expenses. 
(Ord. No. 891, § XI, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-34. - Penalty for violation. 
(a)  Authority. The city shall have the power to administer and enforce the provisions of this article as may be required by governing law. 
(b)  Civil remedies. 
(1)  A property owner violating any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be fined a sum not exceeding $1,000.00 for each and every day of violation, or, if the owner shows the property is the owner's lawful homestead, in an amount not to exceed $10.00 per day for each violation, provided that: 
a.  The owner was notified of the requirements of the article and the owner's need to comply with the requirements; and 
b.  After notification, the owner committed an act in violation of the article or failed to take action necessary for compliance with the article. 
(2)  If such a civil penalty is assessed, the city secretary shall file a certified copy of the order containing such amount and duration of the penalty with the county district clerk's office no later than three working days after such order. 
(c)  Other remedies. 
(1)  The remedies provided herein shall be available to the city in addition to any penal or other remedy provided by law or equity which the city, state, or any other person may provide to remedy the unsafe building condition. 
(2)  The city may bring a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to collect the amount due plus all associated costs and fees. 
(Ord. No. 891, § XII, 10-9-2012)  
Sec. 10-35. - Liability. 
Neither the city nor any authorized agent acting under the terms of this article shall be liable or have any liability by reason of orders issued or work done in compliance with the terms of this article. 
(Ord. No. 891, § XIII, 10-9-2012)  
Secs. 10-36—10-58. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - TECHNICAL CODES  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 10-59—10-89. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - PLUMBING CODE AND PLUMBERS 
 
Sec. 10-90. - Plumbers. 
(a)  A person designated by the state board of plumbing examiners as a responsible master plumber is authorized to submit applications and pull permits relating to the installation, repair, or construction of plumbing components within a building or other structure. A responsible master plumber may designate one person who is authorized to submit applications and pull permits on behalf of the responsible master plumber. A person so designated by a responsible master plumber shall be employed by and under the general supervision of the responsible master plumber, provided that nothing in this section may be construed to require the responsible master plumber to be present when the employee submits an application or pulls a permit. Responsible master plumbers so designating an employee shall submit the employee's name, home address, telephone number, electronic mail address, social security number or state driver's license number to the city plumbing and gas inspector. 
(b)  A responsible master plumber designating an employee under subsection (a) of this section shall notify the city plumbing and gas inspector upon the employee's ceasing to be employed by the responsible master plumber. After such notification, a responsible master plumber may designate a new employee as provided by subsection (a) of this section. 
(Ord. No. 902, 5-14-2013)  
Sec. 10-91. - Plumbing code adopted. 
The book entitled "International Plumbing Code," 2012 edition, and appendices A, B and hereby adopted and hence forth shall be known as the plumbing code for the city. 
(Ord. No. 876, § 1, 5-12-2012)  
Sec. 10-92. - Code revisions adopted. 
The following regulations are hereby adopted for the administration of the plumbing code of the city, and shall be known as chapter 1 of said plumbing code: 
CHAPTER 1 
ADMINISTRATION 
SECTION 101—TITLE AND SCOPE 
101.1—TITLE 
This code shall be known and cited as "The Plumbing Code of the City of Taft," sometimes herein referred to as "the code" or "this code." The portions of this code other than this chapter shall be known as "Part I—Plumbing," which shall be comprised of the book entitled, "International Plumbing Code," 2012 edition, and Appendices A and B and Administration guidelines. 
101.2—CODE REMEDIAL 
101.2.1 GENERAL 
This code is hereby declared to be remedial, and shall be construed to secure the beneficial interest and purpose thereof, which are health, sanitation, general public safety and welfare, by regulating installation and maintenance of all plumbing and consumer's gas piping. 
101.2.2 QUALITY CONTROL 
Quality control of materials and workmanship is not within the purview of this code except as it relates to the purpose stated herein. 
101.2.3 PERMITTING AND INSPECTION 
The inspection or permitting of any building or plan by any jurisdiction, under the requirements of this code shall not be construed is any court as a warranty of the physical condition of such building or the adequacy of such plan. No jurisdiction nor any employee thereof shall be liable in tort for damages for any defect or hazardous or illegal condition or inadequacy in such building or plan, nor for any failure of any component of such building, which may occur subsequent to such inspection or permitting. 
101.3—SCOPE 
101.3.1 APPLICABILITY 
The provisions of this code shall apply to every plumbing and installation, including alterations, repairs, replacement, equipment, appliances, fixtures, fittings, and appurtenances thereto, which is located within the city; and the provisions of this code shall apply to every plumbing and piping installation which is located outside of the city when connected to water, sanitary sewer, or storm sewer of the city. 
101.3.2 FEDERAL AND STATE AUTHORITY 
The provisions of this code shall not be held to deprive any federal or state agency, or any applicable governing body having jurisdiction of any power or authority which it had on the effective date of the adoption of this code or of any remedy then existing for the enforcement of its orders, nor shall it deprive any individual or corporation of its legal rights as provided by law. 
101.3.3 MAINTENANCE 
All plumbing both existing and new, and all parts thereof, shall be maintained in a safe and sanitary condition. All devices or safeguards which are required by this code shall be maintained in good working order. The owner, or his designated agent, if any, shall be responsible for said maintenance. 
101.4—EXISTING BUILDINGS 
101.4.1 GENERAL 
Alterations, repairs or rehabilitation work may be made to any existing building without requiring the building to comply with all the requirements of this code provided that the alteration, repair or rehabilitation work conforms to the requirements of this code for new construction. The building official shall determine the extent to which the existing system shall be made to conform to the requirements of this code for new construction. 
101.4.2 
If, within any period of 12 months, alterations or repairs costing in excess of 50 percent of the then physical value of the building are made to an existing building, such building shall be made to conform to the requirements of this code for new buildings. 
101.4.3 CHANGE OF OCCUPANCY 
If the occupancy classification of an existing building is changed, the building shall be made to conform to the intent of this code as required by the building official. 
SECTION 102—ORGANIZATION 
102.1—BUILDING OFFICIAL AND INSPECTORS 
The plumbing inspector is hereby designated as the person responsible for the administration and enforcement of the plumbing code, and who shall have the authority hereinafter provided for the plumbing official, and the administrative authority. The plumbing inspector may delegate said authority to assistants, inspectors, and other employees of the city that adhere to the states criteria. 
102.2—RESTRICTION ON EMPLOYEES 
No employee of the city shall be financially interested in the furnishing of labor, material, or appliances for the installation, alteration, or maintenance of plumbing installations, or in the making of plans or specifications therefor unless said employee is the owner of the property on which the installation exists or is planned to take place. 
102.3—LIABILITY 
Any officer or employee or member of any board charged with the enforcement of this code, acting for the city in the discharge of duties, shall not thereby be rendered liable personally and is hereby relieved from all personal liability for any damage that may occur to persons or property as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of duties. Any suit brought against any officer or employee because of such act performed in the enforcement of any provision of this code shall be defended by the city's insurance company until the final termination of the proceedings. 
SECTION 103—POWERS AND DUTIES OF BUILDING OFFICIAL 
103.1—RIGHT OF ENTRY 
The plumbing official is authorized to enter any building, structure, or premises to perform any duty imposed by this code. 
103.2—STOP WORK ORDERS 
Upon notice from the plumbing official that work on any plumbing installation is being done contrary to the provisions of this code or in a dangerous or unsafe manner, such work shall be immediately stopped. Such notice shall be in writing and shall be given to the owner of the property, or to his agent, or to the person doing the work, and shall state the conditions under which the work may be resumed. Where any emergency exists, oral notice shall be sufficient. A written determination and record of such emergency notice shall be made by the plumbing official as soon as practicable after discovery of such emergency. 
103.4—REVOCATION OF PERMITS 
103.4.1 MISREPRESENTATION OF APPLICATION 
The plumbing official may revoke a permit or approval, issued under the provisions of this act, in case there has been any false statement or misrepresentation as to a material fact in the application or plans on which the permit or approval was based or whenever the permit or approval was issued in error. 
103.4.2 VIOLATION OF CODE PROVISIONS 
The plumbing official may revoke a permit upon determination by the building official that the construction, erection, alteration, repair, moving or demolition of the building for which the permit was issued is in violation of, or not in conformity with, the provisions of this code. 
103.5—UNSAFE INSTALLATIONS 
All plumbing installations which are unsanitary or which constitute a hazard to human life, health, or welfare are hereby declared illegal and shall be abated by repair or demolition. 
103.6—REQUIREMENTS NOT COVERED BY CODE 
Any requirement necessary for the strength or stability of an existing or proposed building or structure/or for the safety or health of the occupants thereof, not specifically covered by this code, shall be determined by the plumbing or building official. 
103.7—ALTERNATE MATERIALS AND ALTERNATE METHODS 
In case where no applicable accepted standard requirements have been adopted in the code for a given class of appliance, accessory device, material, or method of installation, approval of such class of appliance, accessory device, material or method of installation by the plumbing official. Any application for such approval shall be submitted to the plumbing official and shall include sufficient evidence or proof to reasonably substantiate any claim that may be made regarding the alternate material or method. A list of such approvals shall be maintained on file at the city hall available for inspection by the public during regular working hours. 
104—LOCAL ENVIRONMENTAL, ATMOSPHERIC AND SOIL CONDITIONS 
In consideration of the highly corrosive nature of the atmosphere and soil in the city area, and in consideration of the extreme heaving and shifting characteristics of the soil in the city area, and the city council hereby finding that certain additional standards are necessary to control environmental pollution, the following local standards are established to provide for the public health, safety, and welfare, and the plumbing or code official shall enforce said standards which shall take precedence when in conflict with other standards established by this code: 
(a) Underground water supply systems, water service pipe, and consumer's gas piping shall be at least 18 inches deep. Risers from such water systems, and above ground runs in locations protected from direct exposure to sunlight, may be of the same material approved for use in water systems underground, except that polyvinyl chloride shall be a minimum of schedule 40. 
(b) For water supply control an accessible shut-off valve shall be provided on the water service pipe within five feet of the point where the pipe enters the building. 
(c) Water pumps shall be connected indirectly to the water supply system through the use of water supply tanks and air gaps. An approved reduced pressure principal backflow preventer combined with a pump low pressure cut-off device may be used as an alternate method to connect water pumps provided that engineering plans and specifications detailing the installation accompany the application for permit, and further provided that the owner shall obtain the services of a plumber or manufacturer's representative to inspect and service the installation at intervals not to exceed one year. Fire pumps may be directly connected if approved by the plumbing official.
