Suitable certificates issued for passing an approved examination must be presented to the regulatory authority. Furthermore, each permitted establishment must have "during all hours of operation" a certified food manager on duty. The certified food manager on duty shall have supervisor/management responsibilities with the authority to direct and control food preparation and service. Food manager certificates may be revoked if inspection reveals inadequate sanitation practices. 
(Ord. No. 958, § 8, 8-9-2016)  
Sec. 12-140. - Remedies. 
(a)  Any person who violates a provision of these rules and any person who is the permit holder of or otherwise operates a food service establishment that does not comply with the requirements of these rules and any responsible officer of that permit holder or those persons shall be fined not more than $500.00. 
(b)  The regulatory authority may seek to enjoin violations of these rules. 
(Ord. No. 958, § 9, 8-9-2016)  
Chapter 14 - CEMETERIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Local regulation of cemeteries, V.T.C.A., Health & Safety Code § 713.001 et seq. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 14-1. - Definition; application of chapter. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Cemetery means and includes that cemetery belonging to the city and generally known as the Bellevue Cemetery, and the provisions of this chapter shall apply to such cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 1, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-2. - General supervision. 
The city council grants to the director of public works the necessary authority to execute its orders and to put into effect the rules and regulations prescribed by this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 2, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-3. - Price of lots. 
All lots in the cemetery shall be sold at such price as is set from time to time by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 3, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-4. - Purchase price of lot and other charges must be paid prior to burial. 
The cost for purchase of a lot and for opening and closing of a grave and other final costs for interment may be prepaid in lump sum or by installment. An agreement for installment payment shall be entered into by person making payment and the city. Installments shall be paid in accordance with said agreement and shall be paid in full prior to interment. The city shall deposit prepayment funds in a prepayment account and shall maintain necessary records and pay out said prepaid funds for interment to cemetery operations at time of interment. All charges properly payable to the city must be paid in advance of any interment, except that the city manager may allow interment prior to payment when the costs are to be paid by a funeral home and the funeral home makes contractual arrangements guaranteeing payment. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 4, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-5. - Title to lot not valid until purchase money paid. 
No title to a cemetery lot shall be valid until the amount of the purchase money shall have been paid. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 5, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-6. - General restrictions on use. 
The cemetery shall be used for cemetery purposes only. The city council reserves the right to refuse to sell to, or to allow the burial of any person who, in its judgement, is deemed objectionable. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 6, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-7. - Interment permitted only on order of lot owner. 
The city will not permit any interment to be made on any cemetery lot except under an order from the owner or his heirs, representatives, or assigns, delivered at the office of the director of public works and indicating the desired location for such interment. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 7, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-8. - Lot holders not to allow interments for remuneration. 
Cemetery lot holders shall not allow interments to be made on their lots for a remuneration. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 8, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-9. - When gates to be open. 
The gates of the cemetery will be open from sunrise to sunset to all lot owners and visitors, and shall be closed from sunset to sunrise. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 9, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-10. - Vehicles to be driven slowly and must not turn around in avenues. 
Vehicles must be driven slowly, at a speed not to exceed five miles per hour in the cemetery and must not turn around in the avenues. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 10, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-11. - Vehicle not to be driven or ridden on lots, lawns, or walks; animals shall not be allowed in the cemetery. 
The driving or riding of vehicles will not be allowed on lots or upon the lawns or walks of the cemetery, except vehicles used in the operation and maintenance of the cemetery. Animals shall not be allowed in the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 11, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-12. - Sitting, standing, etc., on lots, graves, monuments, etc. 
Sitting, lounging or lying on lots, mounds, or ornamental grounds at the cemetery and sitting or standing on graves or monuments therein is strictly prohibited, except that the standing or walking on graves by workers in the operation and maintenance of the cemetery and those in attendance at a funeral shall be allowed. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 12, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-13. - Grave digging. 
The digging of a grave for an interment in the cemetery will only be permitted by the city employees. A notice of not less than five working hours must be given to ensure proper preparation of the grave. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 13, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-14. - Changing lot grades. 
The grades of cemetery lots, once established, cannot be changed without the consent of the city council or appointed authority. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 14, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-15. - Signs prohibited. 
Signs indicating that a lot is for sale shall not be permitted in the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 15, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-16. - Order and permit for work on lots. 
The city will not allow work of any description to be placed upon any cemetery lot, unless a written order from the lot holder or his representative is presented and a permit is obtained from the director of public works. This section applies to the cutting of inscriptions, setting of markers, etc., and also to the removal of anything from the lot. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 16, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-17. - Permit for workman. 
No workman, except one employed in the erection of stone work under a regular permit, will be allowed to work in the grounds of the cemetery, except by special permit from the city. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 17, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-18. - Exclusion of persons from grounds; refusal of permits. 
The city authorities shall have the right to exclude from the grounds of the cemetery any person who disobeys any provision of this chapter. They shall also have the right to refuse permits to persons or firms whose work is not satisfactory, or whose employees disobey the rules of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 18, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-19. - Work orders are subject to council rules. 
All orders taken for work in the cemetery shall be subject to the rules of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 19, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-20. - Prohibited enclosures, curbing, ornaments, walks, etc. 
Enclosures of any kind, curbing or coping around a lot, ornaments, chairs, settees, vases, glass jars, pitchers, artificial flowers, flowers, toys, watering cans or other articles that may be considered objectionable by the authorities are prohibited in the cemetery and the right to remove the same without notice to lot owners is reserved. Objects of wood of any kind will not be permitted in the cemetery, and no gravel, brick, stone, cement or other kind of artificial walk will be allowed on any lot. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 20, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-21. - Authority of council to lay out and alter walks and avenues and make rules and regulations. 
The city council or appointed authority may, from time to time, lay out and alter avenues or walks and make such rules and regulations for the government of the grounds and care and control of the lots in the cemetery as they may deem requisite and proper to secure and promote the general objects of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 21, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-22. - Boundary markers to remain undisturbed. 
All boundary markers set up in the cemetery by the city authorities must remain undisturbed. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 22, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-23. - Marker plans to be submitted to city. 
Plans for markers must be submitted to the city to secure permit for erection in the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 23, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-24. - Markers to be in accord with filed plans. 
All markers in the cemetery shall be in accordance with plans on file with the city. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 24, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-25. - Above-ground mausoleums, vaults, or tombs prohibited. 
No special authority will be granted for the erection of mausoleums or vaults or tombs above the grounds, and no such mausoleums, vaults, or tombs shall be erected. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 25, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-26. - Loud conversation prohibited; workmen to cease operations during interment. 
Loud conversation in the cemetery shall not be permitted and all workmen must cease operations while in the immediate vicinity of an interment. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 26, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-27. - City not responsible for articles placed on lots or graves. 
The city will not be responsible for any funeral design, floral pieces, or other article or thing placed on any lot or grave in the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 27, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-28. - Right of city to remove and plant trees and shrubs and mow grass. 
If any trees or shrubs situated on any cemetery lot shall, by mean of their roots or branches, become detrimental to the adjacent lots or avenues, or become unsightly or inconvenient for visitors, it shall be the duty of the city authorities, and they shall have the right to enter the lot for such purpose, to remove the trees or shrubbery or such part thereof as they determine to be unsightly or inconvenient. The city authorities shall have the right to remove any trees or shrub that may be infected by scales or other diseases and to plant and mow the grass on all lots and graves. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 28, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-29. - Removal of funeral designs and floral pieces. 
Funeral designs and floral pieces will be removed from the graves when they become wilted and unsightly. Persons desiring to retain any such design or piece must remove the same within 48 hours after the interment. In no case will employees attempt to locate designs or floral pieces after their removal from the lots. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 29, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-30. - Right of city authorities to fill and level graves and plant grass thereon. 
The cemetery authorities shall have full right to fill and level graves and plant grass thereon, when desired. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 30, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-31. - Material to be moved on paths or planks. 
All materials must be moved on the paths of the cemetery and over planks laid for the purpose, and not over adjoining lots. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 31, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-32. - Right of council to prohibit erection of markers and monuments. 
The city council or appointed authority may prohibit erection of markers and monuments as they may deem requisite and proper to secure and promote the general objectives of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 32, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-33. - Removal of offensive monuments, etc. 
If any monument or any structure, whatever is placed in or upon any cemetery lot which is determined by the authorities of the cemetery to be offensive, improper or injurious to the appearance of the surrounding lots or grounds, they shall have the right, and it shall be their duty to enter upon such lot and remove the offensive or improper object and they may do so without notice to the owner. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 33, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-34. - Responsibility of undertakers for conduct of employees. 
Undertakers will be held responsible for the action of all vehicle drivers or others employed by them while within the grounds of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 34, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-35. - Suspension of work when chapter violated. 
The city shall have the power to suspend work in the cemetery immediately whenever there is a failure to conform to the rules and regulations prescribed in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 35, 2-19-1991)  
Sec. 14-36. - Penalty. 
Any person, firm or corporation who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects, or refuses to comply with, or who resists the enforcement of any of the rules and regulations of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined not more than $200.00 for each offense. Each day that a violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 588, § 36, 2-19-1991)  
Secs. 14-37—14-60. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - CEMETERY MEMORIAL FUND 
 
Sec. 14-61. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Cemetery means and refers to that certain 20 acres of land, more or less, described by the official map (1967) of Bellevue Cemetery, now the Taft Cemetery, and the official map being a composite map of the Bellevue Cemetery showing all of the plats that have been filed on record in the plat records of the county, and according to the office records of the city (successor to Taft Cemetery Association). 
Cemetery improvements means capital improvements only, and shall not include the day-to-day care and upkeep of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 591, § 1, 4-9-1991)  
Sec. 14-62. - Creation of cemetery memorial fund. 
(a)  There is created by this article a cemetery memorial fund for cemetery improvements to the city cemetery, formerly the Bellevue Cemetery. 
(b)  The city is authorized and empowered to receive grants, gifts, and donations from any source for cemetery improvements. 
(Ord. No. 591, § 2, 4-9-1991)  
Sec. 14-63. - Contributions; acknowledgements; expenditures, budgeting and investments; recordkeeping of cemetery memorial fund. 
(a)  A person, association, or corporation may contribute or donate money or property to the city for cemetery improvements. If property, other than money, is donated the city shall have the right to liquidate the property, in its discretion, notwithstanding any contrary provisions contained in the terms of any donative instrument. 
(b)  Acknowledgement of contributions on gifts shall be made to all contributors by a numbered receipt showing the contributor's name, address, amount, and date. If the contribution or gift is given in honor or memory of one or more, appropriate acknowledgement shall also be made to the family of the one being honored or remembered, mailed to person named by the contributor to the address provided. 
(c)  Expenditures shall be made for cemetery improvements by the city only in accordance with the city's cemetery memorial fund budget. The city shall have the right, power, and authority to invest and reinvest all funds and the proceeds of property other than money advanced or contributed to it for the purposes herein specified. 
(d)  The city secretary shall maintain a permanent record of all contributors and additional information the city may deem necessary or proper and shall be responsible for all acknowledgements. 
(Ord. No. 591, § 3, 4-9-1991)

ARTICLE II. - JUDGES 
 
Sec. 16-23. - Municipal court judge to be appointed. 
There shall be appointed for the city a judge for the municipal court of the city, such persons so appointed pursuant to state law. 
(Ord. No. 416, § 1, 2-14-1978)  
Sec. 16-24. - Holding office for term. 
All persons appointed under this article to serve as judge of the municipal court of the city shall hold their terms of office for their term appointed as described herein and until their successors have been appointed and qualified. 
(Ord. No. 416, § 3, 2-14-1978)  
Sec. 16-25. - State laws applicable. 
All laws of the state and ordinances of the city pertaining to judges of municipal courts and the judge of the municipal court of the city shall remain in full force and effect and specifically all laws and statutes requiring oath of office and qualification and training shall be applicable to any judge appointed pursuant to the terms of this article. 
(Ord. No. 416, § 6, 2-14-1978)

ARTICLE III. - FEES AND COSTS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 16-54—16-79. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - JUVENILE CASE MANAGER FUND 
 
Sec. 16-80. - Cost payable upon conviction. 
A defendant convicted of a fine-only misdemeanor offense in the municipal court is required to pay a juvenile case manager fee not to exceed $5.00 as a cost of court. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 2, 1-10-2006)  
Sec. 16-81. - Waiver of case manager fee. 
The municipal court judge is authorized to waive the juvenile case manager fee in a case of financial hardship. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 3, 1-10-2006)  
Sec. 16-82. - Status as convicted. 
A defendant is considered convicted if: 
(1)  A sentence is imposed on the defendant; 
(2)  The defendant receives deferred disposition, including deferred proceedings under Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 45.052 or 45.053. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 4, 1-10-2006)  
Sec. 16-83. - Collection of cost. 
The clerk of the municipal court shall collect the cost and pay them to the municipal treasurer or to any individual commonly delegated as the municipal treasurer for deposit in the fund. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 5, 1-10-2006)  
Sec. 16-84. - Use of fund. 
The fund created under this division will be used only to finance the salary and benefits of the juvenile case manager employed under Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 45.056. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 6, 1-10-2006)  
Sec. 16-85. - Administration of fund. 
The juvenile case manager fund will be administered under the direction of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 7, 1-10-2006)  
Sec. 16-86. - State law adopted by reference. 
The provisions of Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 102.0174 are hereby adopted. 
(Ord. No. 775, § 1, 1-10-2006)  
Chapter 18 - ELECTIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Candidates for municipal office, V.T.C.A., Election Code § 143.001 et seq.; elections, V.T.C.A., Election Code § 1.01 et seq.; conduct of elections, V.T.C.A., Election Code § 61.001 et seq. 
 
Sec. 18-1. - State law applicable. 
All elections pertaining to municipal affairs shall be governed by the election laws of the state. 
(Ord. No. 127, § 1, 2-28-1950)  
Sec. 18-2. - Application for ballot. 
Any eligible and qualified person may have his name printed upon the official ballot as a nonpartisan candidate for the office of mayor, councilmember or other city office by filing his sworn application with the mayor at least 30 days prior to the election day. The application shall state the specific office or place being sought by the applicant and that the applicant is eligible and qualified under the laws of the state to become a candidate for and hold the office being sought, if elected. 
(Ord. No. 127, § 2, 2-28-1950)  
Sec. 18-3. - Withdrawal of candidacy. 
Any person eligible to the office of mayor, commissioner, or other for office who has filed his sworn application in accordance with the provisions of this section shall have his name printed on the official ballots. Any such person may cause his name to be withdrawn at any time before the official ballots are actually printed, by filing in writing with the city secretary a request to that effect over his own signature, duly attested to by a notary public. No name so withdrawn shall be printed on the ballots. Not later than 20 days before the city general election, the city secretary shall have the official ballots printed. 
(Ord. No. 127, § 5, 2-28-1950)  
Chapter 20 - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Texas Disaster Act of 1975, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 418.001 et seq.; municipal programs, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 418.103; local planning required, 37 Tex. Admin. Code § 7.12; local government responsibility, 37 Tex. Admin. Code § 7.23; requesting state assistance, 37 Tex. Admin. Code § 7.24; local government control affirmed, 37 Tex. Admin. Code § 7.26. 
 
Sec. 20-1. - City committee established. 
There is hereby created the municipal emergency management and disaster relief committee which shall consist of the following: 
(1)  The mayor, who shall serve as chairperson of the committee, and who shall also be known as municipal emergency management director. 
(2)  The emergency management coordinator of the city, who shall be charged with the preparation of an emergency management plan for the city, together with such other duties as the director may prescribe. The coordinator shall be appointed by and hold his position at the pleasure of the emergency management director. The coordinator shall serve as vice-chairperson of the municipal emergency management and disaster relief committee. 
(3)  The directors of divisions and chiefs of services of such divisions as may be provided for by resolution by the city council or by direction of the municipal emergency management director. 
(4)  Representatives from civic, business, industry, labor, veterans, professional, or other groups, to be selected and appointed by the mayor. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 1, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-2. - Committee powers and duties. 
(a)  The powers and duties of the municipal emergency management and disaster relief committee shall include the recommendation for adoption by the city council of a emergency management plan for the city, and the recommendation for adoption by the city council of any and all mutual aid plans and agreements which are deemed essential for the implementation of such emergency management plan. 
(b)  The duties of such emergency management and disaster relief committees shall also include the making of a survey of the availability of existing personnel, equipment, supplies and services which could be used during an emergency, as provided for herein, as well as a continuing study of the need for amendments and improvements in the emergency management plan adopted by the city council. The emergency management and disaster relief committee of the city, shall meet upon the call of either the director or coordinator. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 2, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-3. - Joint planning. 
The mayor of the city is hereby authorized to join with the county judge, and the mayors of other cities in the county in the formation of a emergency management and disaster relief council for the county and shall have the authority to cooperate in the formation of a emergency management plan for the county and in the appointment of a emergency management coordinator for the county, as well as all other powers necessary to participate in a county wide program of emergency management and disaster relief insofar as said program may affect the city. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 3, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-4. - Emergency management director. 
(a)  The office of municipal emergency management director is hereby created. The municipal emergency management director shall have the authority to request the declaration of the existence of an emergency by the city council or higher authority. In the event it is deemed necessary to declare the existence of an emergency without delay, the director may, if the city council is not in session, do so, but such action shall be subject to confirmation by the city council at its next meeting. 
(b)  The duties and responsibilities of the municipal emergency management director shall include the following: 
(1)  The control and direction of the actual operation or training efforts of the emergency management and disaster relief organization of the city; 
(2)  The determination of all questions of authority and responsibility that may arise within the emergency management and disaster relief organization of the city; 
(3)  The maintenance of necessary liaison with other municipal, district, state, county, regional, federal, or other emergency management organizations; 
(4)  The marshaling, after declaration of an emergency as provided for above, of all necessary personnel, equipment or supplies from any department of the city to aid in the carrying out of the emergency management plan; 
(5)  The issuance of all necessary proclamations as to the existence of an emergency and the immediate operational effectiveness of the emergency management plan; 
(6)  The issuance of reasonable rules, regulations or directives which are necessary for the protection of life and property in the city, such rules and regulations shall be filed in the office of the city secretary and shall receive widespread publicity unless publicity will be of aid and comfort to the enemy; 
(7)  The supervision of the drafting and execution of mutual aid agreements, in cooperation with the representatives of the state and of other local political subdivisions of the state, and the drafting and execution, if deemed desirable, of an agreement with the county in which said city is located and with other municipalities within the county, for the county-wide coordination of efforts in defense and disaster relief; 
(8)  The supervision of and final authorization for the procurement of all necessary supplies and equipment, including acceptance of private contributions; and 
(9)  The authorizing of agreements, after approval of the city attorney, for the use of private property for public shelter and other purposes. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 4, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-5. - Organization composition. 
The operational emergency management and disaster relief organization of the city shall consist of the officers and employees of the city designated by the municipal emergency management director as well as all volunteer municipal emergency management workers. The functions and duties of this organization shall be distributed among such divisions, services and special staff as the city council shall prescribe by resolution or the municipal emergency management director shall provide by directive. Any such resolution or directive shall set forth the form of organization, establish and designate divisions and services, assign functions, duties and powers, and designate officers and employees to carry out the provisions of this chapter. Insofar as possible, the form of organization, titles, and terminology shall conform to the recommendations of the State Emergency Response Committee (SERC) of the state and the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA). 
(Ord. No. 644, § 5, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-6. - Oath for committee members and others. 
Each person serving as a member of the municipal emergency management and disaster relief committee, or as an officer, employee or volunteer in any capacity in the municipal emergency management and disaster relief organization created by resolution or directive pursuant to the authority herein conferred shall, prior to assuming their duty or duties, take an oath which shall be substantially as follows: 
"I, ___________, do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I have not directly or indirectly paid, offered, or promised to pay, contributed, or promised to contribute any money, or valuable thing, or promised any public office or employment, as a reward to secure my appointment or confirmation thereof, so help me God. I do further solemnly swear (or affirm) that I will faithfully execute the duties of the office to which I am appointed, and will to the best of my ability preserve, protect, and defend the Constitution and laws of the United States and of this state, so help me God." 
(Ord. No. 644, § 6, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-7. - Wrongful operation of warning signal. 
Any unauthorized person who shall operate a siren or other device so as to simulate a warning signal, or the termination of a warning, shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this section and shall be subject to the penalties imposed by this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 7, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-8. - Priority of regulations. 
At all times when the orders, rules and regulations made and promulgated pursuant to this chapter shall be in effect, they shall supersede all existing ordinances, orders, rules and regulations insofar as the latter may be inconsistent therewith. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 8, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-9. - Interpretation. 
This chapter shall not be construed so as to conflict with any state or federal statute or with any military or naval order, rule or regulation. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 9, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-10. - Liability. 
This chapter is an exercise by the city of its governmental functions for the protection of the public peace, health and safety and neither the city, the agents and representatives of said city, or any individual, receiver, firm, partnership, corporation, association, or trustee, or any of the agents thereof, in good faith carrying out, complying with or attempting to comply with, any order, rule, or regulation promulgated pursuant to the provisions of this article shall be liable for any damage sustained to persons or property as the result of said activity. Any person owning or controlling real estate or other premises who voluntarily and without compensation grants to the city a license or privilege, or otherwise permits the city to inspect, designate and use the whole or any part of such real estate for the purpose of sheltering persons during an actual impending or practice enemy attack shall, together with his successor in interest, if any, not be civilly liable for the death of, injury to, any person on or about such real estate or premises under such license, privileges or other permission or for loss of, or damage to, the property of such person. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 10, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-11. - Funding of emergency management activities. 
No person shall have the right to expend any public funds of the city in carrying out any emergency management activity authorized by this article without prior approval by the city council, nor shall any person have the right to bind the city by contract, agreement or otherwise without prior and specific approval of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 11, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-12. - Unlawful obstruction. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully obstruct, hinder, or delay any member of the emergency management organization in the enforcement of any rule or regulation issued pursuant to this chapter, or to do any act forbidden by any rules or regulation issued pursuant to the authority contained in this chapter. It shall likewise be unlawful for any person to wear, carry or display any emblem, insignia or any other means of identification as a member of the emergency management organization, except as authorized by the proper official. Convictions for violations of the provisions of this article shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed $200.00 upon conviction. 
(Ord. No. 644, § 12, 10-8-1996)  
Sec. 20-13. - NIMS adopted. 
The city adopts the National Incident Management System dated March 1, 2004. 
(Ord. No. 759, 7-12-2005)  
Sec. 20-14. - Volunteer corporation is autonomous entity. 
The Taft Volunteer Emergency Medical Service, Inc., a nonprofit corporation, is an entity autonomous from the city. 
(Ord. No. 849, § 4, 5-25-2010)  
Chapter 22 - ENVIRONMENT AND NUISANCES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Municipal power concerning weeds and other unsanitary matter, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.004; assessment of expenses and lien for abatement by municipality, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.007; persons not to permit abandoned property to become public health nuisance, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 341.013(e); junked vehicles as nuisance, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.072; abatement of nuisance of junked vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 683.071—683.078. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 22-1—22-18. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - NUISANCE ABATEMENT[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 953, adopted May 10, 2016, amended article II in its entirety to read as herein set out. Formerly, article II, divisions 1—6 pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Ord. No. 875, adopted April 10, 2012. 
 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 22-19. - Title. 
The following provisions shall be and constitute the Taft nuisance abatement ordinance addressing property and environmental safety. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-20. - Statutory references. 
V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code §§ 342.001—342.007 
V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code §§ 365.001—465.015 
V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 54.001—54.019 
V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 54.011—54.019 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-21. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this article represents an aggregated number of causes to eliminate; stagnant water; litter; and debris throughout the city. Said conditions; breed disease; rodents; fire hazards and compromise the citizen's quality of life, property values and investments. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-22. - Definitions. 
Approved citizens collection station. See division 7. 
Brush means decaying remains of cut or broken vegetation. 
Code enforcement official means the designated authority charged with the enforcement of this article, or his duly authorized representative. 
Cultivated includes but is not limited to tending, maintaining, and removal of litter and brush. 
Dispose means to discharge, deposit, bury, spill, leak, or place litter on or into land or water. 
Improved lot means a lot on which a structure is located. 
Litter means: 
(1)  Decayed waste from a public or private establishment, residence, or restaurant, including yard trimmings, leaves or similar materials, animals and vegetation, waste material from a market or storage facility handling or storing produce, other food products, but not including sewage, body wastes, or industrial by-products, or 
(2)  Non-decayable solid waste: 
a.  Combustible waste material, including paper, rags, cartons, wood, furniture, rubber and plastics; 
b.  Noncombustible waste material, including glass, crockery, tin or aluminum cans, metal furniture, and similar materials that do not burn at ordinary incinerator temperatures of 1,800 degrees Fahrenheit or less; and 
c.  Discarded or worn-out manufactured materials and machinery, including motor vehicles and parts of motor vehicles, tires, aircraft, farm implements, building or construction materials, appliances, and scrap metal. 
Lot means any piece or parcel of land or a portion of a sub division, the boundaries of which have been established by legal instrument of record. 
Maintain means to provide for upkeep or support; to keep unimpaired or in proper condition. 
Person means an individual, corporation, organization, government, business trust, partnership, association, or other legal entity. 
Sanitary means a condition of good order and cleanliness that precludes the probability of disease transmission. 
Shrub means all trees or shrubbery less than four feet in height with trunk or stems less than two inches in diameter which are not maintained, cared for, or cultivated. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-23. - Administrative liability. 
No officer, agent, or employee of the city shall be personally liable for any damage that may accrue to persons or property as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of his duties under this article. Any suit brought against any officer, agent or employee of the city as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of his duties under this article shall be defended by the city until the final determination of the proceedings. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-24—22-50. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - PUBLIC NUISANCES 
 
Sec. 22-51. - Unlawful. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, permit or allow a public nuisance as herein defined to exist or remain on any premises under their control. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-52. - Stagnant water. 
Accumulations of water which may attract or harbor mosquitoes or produce disease are hereby declared a public nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-53. - Unsanitary conditions. 
Unwholesome, impure or unsanitary conditions that may produce disease or are likely to attract or harbor insects, rodents, vermin, snakes or disease carrying pests are hereby declared a public nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-54. - Vacant lots not exempted. 
Vacant lots in their natural state that share a common boundary with an improved lot shall be maintained by its owner of record so as to address the requirements specified in section 22-21 under "purpose." 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-55. - Litter. 
Accumulations of litter are hereby declared a public nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-56. - Compost piles. 
Personal compost piles which are maintained and kept for residential use are encouraged and are exempt. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-57. - Brush and bulky items. 
(a)  The city will collect, once a month (obtain schedule of pickup from the City of Taft), from active residential customers, old furniture, appliances, junk, and bulk items placed at the curb on regular brush/bulk collection schedule. Materials shall be placed for pick up no more than three days prior to scheduled pickup. The following residential uses are not provided bulk pick up: 
(1)  Apartments with more than two units. 
(2)  No material generated at a location other than the residence from which it is collected shall be placed in any place or pile for pick up and disposal. 
(3)  No material generated by a hired, commercial, or contracted person or service shall be placed in any place or pile for pick up and disposal. 
(4)  No boards, lumber, drywall, or other building and remodeling materials shall be placed in any place or pile for pick up and disposal. Small quantities can be brought to the collection station. 
(5)  All persons utilizing the services must: 
a.  Place only materials in the place specified on or adjacent to his or her property (or the property managed, rented, or occupied by him or her) only. 
b.  Place no more than six cubic yards of brush or bulky items per monthly collection. Small amounts can be disposed of in your garbage container. 
c.  Items that cannot be effectively disposed of in the garbage container shall be placed behind the street curb within eight feet of the curb line of the street. Items should not be placed under any low wires or limbs and shall be placed at least six feet from any other objects (mailboxes, cars, garbage containers, etc.). Items placed in violation of this provision shall constitute a request for service. 
d.  Items placed out at the curb on non-collection days or non-compliant items placed at the curb will constitute a request for service for which a special pickup charge of $100.00 per six cubic yards will be assessed. By requesting this service, the resident will be charged the fee and it will be added to your City of Taft utility bill. The additional fee will be effective October 1, 2016. 
(b)  Enforcement. 
(1)  No person shall violate the terms of this section and enforcement may be taken against any person who violates the terms of this section. Enforcement is in addition to any charges assessed to the property for items being removed and properly disposed. 
(2)  Additionally, failure to comply with the terms of this section shall he deemed to be-a public nuisance. 
(3)  Any materials placed out for collection shall be presumed to belong to and be the responsibility of the utility customer, owner, manager, tenant, or occupant of any dwelling, building, or premises in front of which, or adjacent to which, the materials are placed. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-58—22-80. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - HEALTH AND SAFETY CODE 
 
Sec. 22-81. - Notice to abate public nuisance. 
The code enforcement official shall give written notice to the owner of a lot to abate a violation found on the premises. The notice shall require the abatement of the violation within ten days of the date of the notice. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-82. - Method of notice. 
Method of notice must be given: 
(1)  Personally, to the owner in writing; 
(2)  By letter addressed to the owner at the owner's post office address; or 
(3)  By letter addressed to the owner at the owner's address as recorded in the appraisal records of the appraisal district in which the property is located; or 
a.  If personal service cannot be obtained: 
1.  By publication at least once; 
2.  By posting the notice on or near the front door of each building on the property to which the violation relates; or 
3.  By posting the notice on a placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates. 
(4)  If the United States Postal Service returns the notice sent to a property owner in accordance with subsection (2) as "refused" or "unclaimed," the validity of the notice is not affected, and the notice is considered as delivered. 
(5)  Notice under subsection (2) shall also inform the property owner(s) that another violation of the same kind or nature that poses a danger to the public health and safety on or before the first anniversary of the date of the notice, the city, without further notice, will correct the violation at the owner's expense against the property. If a violation covered by a notice under this subsection occurs within the one-year period, and the city has not been informed in writing, without notice, will take any action permitted by subsections (1)a. and b., and assess its expenses as provided by V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.007. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-83. - Abatement by city. 
If the owner of the property does not comply with the requirements of a notice to abate a violation, the city may perform or cause to be performed the work or improvements required. The city may pay for the work done or improvements made and charge the expenses to the owner of the property as outlined in division 4. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-84—22-100. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 4. - ASSESSMENT OF EXPENSES; LIEN 
 
Sec. 22-101. - Assessment. 
Required work or improvements performed or cause to be performed by the city shall be charged to the owner of the property. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-102. - Established fees. 
Administrative fees 	$100.00 per case 
Backhoe (1.75 Yd.) 	$40.00 per hour 
Utility truck 	$25.00 per hour 
Half-ton truck 	$25.00 per hour 
Dump truck (10 Yd.) 	$50.00 per hour 
Flatbed truck 	$25.00 per hour 
Brush truck 	$60.00 per hour 
Pickup truck 	$25.00 per hour 
Personnel—Laborer 	$15.00 per hour 
Personnel—Supervisor 	$25.00 per hour 
Backhoe operator 	$25.00 per hour 
Dump/brush truck driver 	$20.00 per hour 
Small equipment 	$10.00 per hour 
 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-103. - Expenses. 
Related expenses shall include but are not limited to the costs of inspection or testing by third parties, photography, publication costs, title search fees, attorney's fees, costs incurred in identifying, locating, or contacting the owner, landfill fees, etc. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-104. - Invoice. 
The code enforcement official shall certify the expense incurred in enforcing the provisions of this article for invoicing to the owner of the property. The invoice becomes an account receivable upon completion and shall be due within 30 days of invoicing. The invoice shall be delivered personally or by certified mailed to the owner's address at post office address. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-105. - Lien after certification. 
If personal service cannot be obtained or the owner's post office address is unknown, the lien may be filed after certification of the expenses. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-106. - Lien. 
If payment in full has not been received after 30 days from invoicing, the city shall assess the expenses against the property in the form of a lien. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-107. - Execution of lien. 
The mayor, or other city official designated by the mayor, shall execute the lien on behalf of the city. The lien shall be filed with the county clerk. The lien arises and attaches to the property at the time the lien is recorded and indexed in the office of the county clerk. The lien should contain the name of the owner, a legal description of the real property, the amount of expenses incurred by the city, the interest rate to be charged, and the balance due. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-108. - Lien priveleged. 
The city's lien is a privileged lien subordinate only to tax liens and liens for street improvements. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-109. - Release of lien. 
The lien shall be extinguished and released if the city is reimbursed for the total amount due. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-110. - Foreclosure. 
The city may authorize its attorney to bring a suit of foreclosure of lien in the name of the city to recover expenditures and interest due. Such suit may be filed in any court having jurisdiction over such matter, against any property for which such bill has remained unpaid 60 days after it has been rendered. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-111—22-130. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 5. - PROHIBITED ACTS 
 
Sec. 22-131. - Obstruction. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct or interfere with the implementation of any action required by the order of the code enforcement official. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-132. - Disposal of litter. 
It shall be unlawful to dispose or allow or permit the disposal of litter at a place that is not an approved solid waste site, including a place on or within 300 feet of a public highway, on a right-of-way, or other public or private property. (Refer to V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 365.012) 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-133. - Receive litter. 
It shall be unlawful to receive litter for disposal at a place that is not an approved solid waste site. (Refer to V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 365.012) 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-134. - Transport litter. 
It shall be unlawful for a person to transport litter to a place that is not an approved solid waste site for disposal at the site. (Refer to V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 365.012) 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-135. - Public nuisance. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, permit or allow a public nuisance as herein defined to exist or remain on any premises in the city. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-136—22-160. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 6. - ENFORCEMENT AND REMEDIES 
 
Sec. 22-161. - Criminal. 
Any person who violates any provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor (Class C), and upon conviction shall be fined $200.00 on the first offense, $400.00 fine on the second offense and up to $1,000.00 for the third or more offense. Each day such violation exists shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-162. - Disposal of litter. 
Certain violations specified in sections 22-132—22-134 of this article may be classified as Class C, B, or A misdemeanors, or third degree felonies. Consult V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 365, subch. B. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-163. - Civil. 
The city may direct its attorney to bring a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to enforce the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-164—22-180. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 7. - CITIZEN'S COLLECTION STATION POLICIES AND FEES 
 
Sec. 22-181. - Location. 
501 Industrial 
Taft, Texas 78390 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-182. - Hours of operation. 
Tuesday: 1:00 p.m.—4:30 p.m. 
First Saturday of every month: 9:00 a.m.—1:00 p.m. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-183. - Purpose. 
The Citizens Collection Station is provided for the convenience and exclusive use of residents/businesses to dispose of solid waste items which they would have normally taken to a landfill. It is not meant to be used for disposal of regular household and kitchen garbage, but instead for disposal of other than usual solid waste items homeowners/businesses sometimes need to dispose of. These items might include the larger than normal items the person wants to dispose of rather than placing them in front of their house for curbside collection. Some examples include furniture, mattresses, used clothing, old appliances, or debris from a homeowner's remodeling job. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-184. - Prohibited users. 
(a)  A person, or company, collecting solid waste items for someone else in exchange for a fee. 
(b)  A person, or company, transporting debris generated by themselves at a worksite where they are being paid to work. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-185. - Prohibited items. 
(a)  Organic household waste which may generate odor during decomposition, or attract rodents or flies. 
(b)  Brush or tree limbs of all sizes. 
(c)  Dead animals or slaughterhouse wastes. 
(d)  Used tires and oil filters. 
(e)  Wastewater treatment plant sludge, septic tank waste, or grease and grit trap wastes. 
(f)  Burned material. 
(g)  Batteries. 
(h)  Discarded materials containing asbestos. 
(i)  Any devices containing. Freon unless they have been drained of Freon and tagged by a certified inspector. 
(j)  Hazardous waste as defined by the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) pursuant to the federal Solid Waste Disposal Act as amended by the Resource Conservation and Recovery Act, 42 USC 6901 et. seq., as amended. 
(k)  Metal and plastic containers may be accepted if they are clean and dry, and the lids or bottoms removed. 
(l)  Roof debris (shingles, felt paper, etc.) shall not be accepted in quantities exceeding one pick-up load. 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Sec. 22-186. - Fees. 
(a)  Citizens/businesses are allowed to dispose of one load of the equivalent of two cubic yards (4'x6'x2' filled level) at no charge upon presentation of their receipt for payment of city utility services. This shall apply to all acceptable items with the exception of roof debris (see subsection (f)). The receipt must be marked as paid within the last 30 days. Residents will need to present identification to city hall staff, the address on which must match the utility account service address in order to dispose of debris at no charge. Business employees must present a current employee identification card. If the driver's license address does not match the utility account service address, citizen must present copy of the account holders identification card along with a contact phone number that staff can call and verify permission to dispose. If resident has neither of these, the city manager will make the final decision. 
(b)  $10.00 minimum fee for small loads up to two cubic yards. 
(c)  $20.00 fee for trucks or trailers containing up to three cubic yards (approximately 4'x6'x4' high). 
(d)  $40.00 fee for trucks or trailers containing up to four cubic yards (approximately 4'x9'x3' high). 
(e)  Loads exceeding four cubic yards shall be charged the equivalent of $15.00/cy. 
(f)  $30.00/cy for any roof debris (limited to one cubic yard per customer). 
(Ord. No. 953, 5-10-2016; Ord. No. 957, 8-9-2016; Ord. No. 970, 5-9-2017; Ord. No. 1033, 5-28-2019)  
Secs. 22-187—22-214. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - NOISE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Type A municipality may regulate certain noises, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 217.003(d); restricted regulation of sport shooting ranges, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 250.001. 
 
Sec. 22-215. - Permit for playing musical instrument on street or sidewalk. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to play upon any kind of musical instrument upon any of the streets or sidewalks of the city, unless a parade or assembly permit has been obtained as required in this article. A permit shall be obtained as outlined in section 22-216. The city manager shall have the authority to waive any or all permit fees for school and chamber of commerce parades only. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 1, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-216. - Permit for operation of vehicle carrying loudspeaker, etc. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive or permit to be operated upon the streets of the city any vehicle carrying loudspeakers or megaphones to which are attached audio equipment or other musical instruments at a time when such megaphones or loudspeakers are emitting sound music or voice, or to drive or permit to be operated upon the streets of the city any vehicle carrying loudspeakers or megaphones through which the human voice is emitted directly or through which the human voice or sound is indirectly emitted by means of mechanical or electrical reproduction and amplification of sound, without first obtaining from the chief of police a written permit thereof. Such permit may be withheld if the volume of sound is such as to disturb persons of ordinary sensibilities in any place for which the permit is sought. A fee of $25.00 shall be paid prior to issuance of a permit. Such permit shall be valid for a period of no more than ten days from the date of issuance. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 2, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-217. - Use of loudspeakers, etc. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or to permit to be operated in any public place or any premises owned, controlled or occupied by him, any mechanical or electrical, musical instrument, loudspeaker or megaphone to which is attached an audio system, or other musical instrument of any nature in such a manner and to such a degree of sound as to disturb or molest the rest, health, or peace of persons occupying premises in the vicinity of the place from which such sound is emitted. The enforcement of this section shall not apply to community events held at schools, churches or institutions scheduled between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. on weekdays and 7:00 a.m. to 11:00 p.m. on Fridays and Saturdays. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 3, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-218. - Vehicle loads producing unreasonably loud sounds. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive along or upon any public street or alley in the city any vehicle, which is loaded with iron or other material likely to produce an unreasonably loud sound without using proper deadening substance to prevent noises disturbing to reasonable persons of ordinary sensibilities within 150 feet of such vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 4, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-219. - Certain acts declared as nuisances; nonexclusive. 
The following acts, among others, are declared to be nuisances in violation of this article, but such enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive: 
(1)  Radios, television sets, musical instruments, and similar devices. The operation or permitting the use or operation of any radio, television, audio system or musical instrument in such a manner or at such volume as to disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of neighboring inhabitants or at a volume which is plainly audible to persons other than those who are in the room in which such device or instrument is played and who are voluntary listeners thereto. 
(2)  Stationary loudspeakers or amplifiers. Except for organized events which have obtained any type of permit from the city in conjunction with the event, no person shall play any radio, music player, television or audio system upon a public right-of-way or upon other public property in such a manner or at such a volume as to disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of other persons. 
(3)  Parties and other social events. It shall be unlawful for any person in charge of a party or other social event to allow that party or event to produce noise in a loud or offensive manner such that the noise interferes with the peace or health of members of the public or is audible through walls between units within the same building, from property or from the street. A person shall be deemed to be in charge of a party or social event when that event occurs on private property and the person is present at the event and is the property owner or has authorization for the use of the premises. 
(4)  Animals and birds. The keeping of any animal or bird, which by causing frequent or long-continued noise shall disturb the comfort and repose of reasonable persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity. 
(5)  Sound devices in motor vehicles. The playing of any radio, music player or audio system in a motor vehicle at such volume as to disturb the quiet, comfort, or repose of other persons or at a volume which is plainly audible to persons other than the occupants of said vehicle. 
(6)  Horns and signal devices on automobiles, etc. The continued or frequent sounding of any horn or signal device of any automobile, motorcycle, bus or other vehicle, except as a danger or warning signal or the creation by means of such signal device of any unreasonably loud or harsh noise for any unnecessary and unreasonable period of time, so as to disturb reasonable persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity. 
(7)  Noise near school, church, etc. The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school or institution of learning or adjacent to any church or institution while the same is in session or which unreasonably interferes with the workings of such institution or church, provided conspicuous signs are displayed in such manner indicating that the same is a school or church, so as to disturb persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity. 
(8)  Loading and unloading operations. The creation of any loud and excessive noise in connection with the loading or unloading of any vehicle, so as to disturb reasonable persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 5, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-220. - Unreasonably loud noises declared a nuisance. 
Any unreasonably loud, disturbing, noise which causes material distress, discomfort or injury to reasonable persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity thereof is hereby declared to be a nuisance and is prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 6, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-221. - Noise of such character as to interfere with enjoyment of homes. 
Any noise of such character, intensity and continued duration as to substantially interfere with the comfortable enjoyment of private homes by reasonable persons of ordinary sensibilities is declared to be a nuisance and is prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 7, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-222. - Penalties. 
Any person guilty of violating any provisions of this article, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not more than $500.00 for each offense. In addition, after a fourth conviction, the equipment or devices which shall include, but are not limited to, compact disc/tape player, stereo receiver, amplifier, pre-amplifier, speakers, and speaker boxes used in the commission of a violation of this article is hereby declared to be contraband and the court shall order that these items be seized and disposed of by the city. Each day any violation shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 741, § 8, 6-8-2004)  
Sec. 22-223. - Engine brakes (Jake Brakes) prohibited. 
(a)  Engine brakes prohibited. 
(1)  Engine brakes. This section applies to the use or operation of an auxiliary or compression engine brake (also known as "Jake Brake") which produces any noise in addition to the normal operating engine noise is prohibited within the city limits. This provision is not intended to prohibit the passage of vehicles equipped with engine brakes or "Jake Brakes" in posted areas but rather prohibit the use of such equipment in posted areas. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for any driver of a truck or truck-tractor to activate or use the unit's engine brake within the city limits except in an emergency situation. 
(3)  The term "emergency situation", for the purposes of this section, shall mean one in which there is imminent danger of collision with property, persons or animals. 
(4)  City-owned and other emergency vehicles are exempt from this section. 
(b)  Penalty. Any person, or persons, violating or failing to comply with any provision of this section shall be fined, upon conviction, not less than $1.00, or more than $500.00, for each offense. 
(Ord. No. 998, § I, 10-9-2018)  
Secs. 22-224—22-250. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - WEEDS, GRASS, AND VEGETATION 
 
Sec. 22-251. - Growth to certain height prohibited; offenses. 
(a)  A person commits an offense if he is an owner, occupant, or person in control of occupied and unoccupied premises in the city; and 
(1)  Permits weeds or grass located on the premises to grow to a height greater than 12 inches, or 
(2)  Fails to remove weeds or grass from the premises after they have been cut. 
(b)  It is a defense to prosecution under: 
(1)  Subsection (a)(1) that the weeds or grass are maintained at or below a height of 12 inches at all points on the premises within 100 feet of its perimeters, and 
(2)  Subsection (a)(2) that the weeds and grass have been mulched, raked, or composted in a manner approved by the director. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-252. - Duty to prevent weeds, grass or vegetation from becoming a nuisance or fire hazard. 
Every owner, occupant, or person in control of any occupied or unoccupied premises in the city shall use every precaution to prevent weeds, grass or other vegetation from growing on the premises so as to become a nuisance or fire hazard. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-253. - Vegetation in alley, street, or sidewalk. 
(a)  An owner, occupant, or person in control of any private premises abutting an alley, street, or sidewalk within the city commits an offense if he allows any vegetation, including, but not limited to, trees, shrubbery, bushes, and vines to grow on the premises so as to project across the property line over or into the right-of-way of the alley, street, or sidewalk. 
(b)  It is a defense to prosecution under subsection (a) that: 
(1)  The vegetation consisted solely of weeds or grass not more than 12 inches high; 
(2)  No part of the vegetation projected over or into the alley or street at a height of less than 15 feet above the ground; or 
(3)  No part of the vegetation projected over or into the sidewalk at a height of less than eight feet above the ground, except that this defense does not apply if the vegetation obstructed the visibility of a traffic control sign, signal, or device or interfered with garbage or trash collection adjacent to the sidewalk. 
(c)  Vegetation growing in violation of this section is a nuisance and may be abated by the city in accordance with section 22-255. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-254. - Enforcement. 
For the purposes of this article, "director" means the director of the department designated by the city manager to enforce and administer this article or the director's authorized representative. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-255. - City removal of weeds and vegetation upon failure of owner, occupant, or person in control to do so; notice required. 
(a)  Upon failure of the owner, occupant or person in control of private premises to comply with section 22-251, the director shall have the weeds or grass cut, mulched, raked, and removed from the premises. 
(b)  Upon the failure of the owner, occupant or person in control of private premises abutting an alley, street, or sidewalk within the city comply with section 22-253, the director shall have the noncomplying vegetation cut or trimmed, and removed from the alley, street, or sidewalk, whichever applies. 
(c)  Before performing work, or causing work to be performed, under subsection (a) or (b), the director must notify the owner of the premises to bring the premises into compliance within seven days. The notice must be in writing and may be served by handing it to the owner in person or by sending it United States regular mail, address to the owner at the owner's address as recorded in the appraisal district records of the appraisal district in which the premises are located. 
(d)  If personal service to the owner cannot be obtained, then the owner may be notified by: 
(1)  Publication at least once in a newspaper of general circulation in the city; 
(2)  Posting the notice on or near the front door of each building on the premises to which the violation relates; or 
(3)  Posting the notice on a placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the premises to which the violation relates. 
(e)  If the director mails a notice to a property owner in accordance with subsection (c), and the United States Postal Service returns the notice as "refused" or "unclaimed", the validity of the notice is not affected, and the notice is considered as delivered. 
(f)  In a notice provided under this section, the director may, by regular mail and by a posting on the property, inform the owner of the property on which the violation exists that, if the owner commits another violation of the same kind or nature that poses a danger to the public health and safety on or before the first anniversary of the date of the notice, the city may, without further notice, correct the violation at the owner's expense and then, in case of a violation of section 22-251, assess the expense against the property. If a violation covered by a notice under this subsection occurs within the one-year period, and the city has not been informed in writing by the owner of a change in ownership, then the city may, without notice, take any action permitted by subsection (a) or (b) and assess its expenses as provided in section 22-256. 
(g)  The director may issue citations and prosecute persons for violating section 22-251 or 22-253 regardless of whether a notice is issued under this section. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-256. - Charges to be collected from the property owner; lien on premises for failure to pay charges. 
(a)  If the city cuts, mulches, rakes, or removes weeds or grass on or from private premises under subsection 22-255(a) or cuts, trims or removes vegetation projecting over or into an alley, street, or sidewalk right-of-way under subsection 22-255(b) (either at the request of the owner or upon the failure of the owner to comply with the notice required under subsection 22-255(c), charges in the amount of the total actual costs incurred by the city in performing the work will be collected from the owner by the city comptroller. If the work was performed under subsection 22-255(a), the charges may be levied, assessed, and collected against the premises on which the work is performed and the city controller shall file a statement by the director with the county clerk of the county in which the property is located setting out the total actual costs incurred by the city, the name of the property owner if known, and a legal description of the property, as required by state law. 
(b)  At the time a statement is filed under subsection (a) for work performed under subsection 22-255(a), as required by state law, the city shall have a privileged lien against the premises, second only to tax liens and liens for street improvements, in the amount of the actual costs incurred, plus ten percent interest on that amount from the date the costs were incurred. 
(c)  The city may file a suit in an appropriate court of law to foreclose upon its lien and recover its actual costs incurred plus interest. The suit may be filed in the name of the city. The statement filed under Subsection (a), or a certified copy of the statement, is prima facie proof of the amount of actual costs incurred by the city. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-257. - Administrative fee. 
The code enforcement department is hereby authorized to assess an administrative fee of $100.00 for actions taken by the city to correct, remove or remedy such conditions in accordance with section 22-255. Said administrative fee shall be added to all other charges incurred by the city. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Sec. 22-258. - Penalty for violation. 
Any violation of this article shall be a Class C misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof, any person violating shall be fined any sum not exceeding $200.00, and each day such violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 939, § 1, 8-25-2015)  
Secs. 22-259—22-275. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - LITTER 
 
Sec. 22-276. - Short title. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as the "City of Taft Anti-Litter Ordinance". 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-277. - Definitions. 
For the purposes of this article, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words used in the present tense include the future, words used in the plural number include the singular number and words used in the singular number include the plural number. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory. 
Aircraft means any contrivance now known or hereafter invented, used or designated for navigation or for flight in the air. The word "aircraft" shall include helicopters and lighter-than-air dirigibles and balloons. 
Authorized private receptacle means a litter storage and collection receptacle as required and authorized by city ordinance. 
City means the City of Taft, Texas. 
Commercial handbill means any printed or written matter, any sample or device, dodger, circular, leaflet, pamphlet, paper, booklet or any other printed or otherwise reproduced original or copies of any matter of literature: 
(1)  Which advertises for sale any merchandise, product, commodity or thing; 
(2)  Which directs attention to any business or mercantile or commercial establishment, or other activity, for the purpose of either directly or indirectly promoting the interest thereof by sales; 
(3)  Which directs attention to or advertises any meeting, theatrical performance, exhibition or event of any kind, for which an admission fee is charged for the purpose of private gain or profit; but the terms of this clause shall not apply where an admission fee is charged or a collection is taken up for the purpose of defraying the expenses incident to such meeting, theatrical performance, exhibition or event of any kind, when either of the same is held, given or takes place in connection with the dissemination of information which is not restricted under the ordinary rules of decency, good morals, public peace, safety and good order. Nothing contained in this clause shall be deemed to authorize the holding, giving or taking place of any meeting, theatrical performance, exhibition or event of any kind without a license, where such license is or may be required by any law of this state, or under any ordinance of this city; or 
(4)  Which, while containing reading matter other than advertising matter, is predominantly and essentially an advertisement, and is distributed or circulated for advertising purposes, or for the private benefit and gain of any person so engaged as advertiser or distributor. 
Director means the director of the department designated by the city manager to enforce and administer this article or the city manager's authorized representative. 
Garbage means putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking and consumption of food. 
Litter means "garbage", "refuse" and "rubbish" as defined herein and all other waste material which, if thrown or deposited as herein prohibited, tends to create a danger to public health, safety and welfare. 
Newspaper means any newspaper of general circulation as defined by general law, any newspaper duly entered with the Post Office Department of the United States, in accordance with federal statute or regulation and any newspaper filed and recorded with any recording officer as provided by general law; and, in addition thereto, any periodical or current magazine regularly published with not less than four issues per year, and sold to the public. 
Noncommercial handbill means any printed or written matter, any sample or device, dodger, circular, leaflet, pamphlet, newspaper, magazine, paper, booklet or any other printed or otherwise reproduced original or copies of any matter of literature not included in the aforesaid definitions of a commercial handbill or newspaper. 
Park means a park, reservation, playground, beach, recreation center or any other public area in the city, owned or used by the city and devoted to active or passive recreation. 
Person means any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or organization of any kind. 
Private premises means any dwelling, house, building or other structure designed or used either wholly or in part for private residential purposes, whether inhabited or temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant, including any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, porch, steps, vestibule or mailbox belonging or appurtenant to such dwelling, house, building or other structure. 
Public place means any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys, or other public ways and any and all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds and buildings. 
Refuse means all putrescible and nonputrescible solid wastes (except body wastes), including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleaning, dead animals, abandoned automobiles, and solid market and industrial wastes. 
Rubbish means nonputrescible solid wastes consisting of both combustible and noncombustible wastes, such as paper, wrappings, cigarettes, cardboard, tin cans, yard clippings, leaves, wood, glass, bedding, crockery and similar materials. 
Vehicle means every device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway, including devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-278. - Throwing or depositing litter in public places prohibited; exceptions. 
No person shall throw or deposit litter in or upon any street, sidewalk or other public place within the city, except in public receptacles, in authorized private receptacles for collection or in official city dumps. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-279. - Manner of placing litter in receptacles. 
Persons placing litter in public receptacles or in authorized private receptacles shall do so in such a manner as to prevent it from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon private property. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-280. - Sweeping litter into gutters, etc. prohibited; sidewalks to be kept free of litter by abutting property owners or occupants. 
No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the city the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying property shall keep the sidewalk in front of their premises free of litter. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-281. - Duty of merchants and contractors as to litter in abutting sidewalks, etc. 
(a)  No person owning or occupying a place of business shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the city the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying places of business within the city shall keep the sidewalk in front of their business premises free of litter. 
(b)  A person doing construction work within the city shall at all times keep the sidewalk, street, alley and public or private property abutting the construction site free of construction trash, litter and debris. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-282. - Throwing litter from vehicles prohibited. 
No person, while a driver or passenger in a vehicle, shall throw or deposit litter upon any street or other public place within the city, or upon private property. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-283. - Removal of injurious material from streets. 
A person who drops or throws or permits to be dropped or thrown upon a street any destructive or injurious material, shall immediately remove the material or cause the material to be removed. 
(Ord. No. 943, § 1, 10-13-2015)  
Sec. 22-284. - Litter in parks.
